Important Telegrams

Central Supervisory Committee Approves Expulsion of Traitorous Party Members

(Nanjing) The Central Supervisory Committee held its 16th temporary meeting on the 23rd. Among the supervisory committee members present were Lin Sen and several others. Resolutions were passed regarding several cases of party discipline, the most important of which was the expulsion of traitorous party members such as Zhao Xinbo who participated in the puppet organizations in Northeast China. (Central News Agency dispatch, 23rd)

Measures for Relocated Tax Collection by Customs in Northeast China

(Nanjing) The Executive Yuan has resolved that all measures regarding the relocation of tax collection by customs in Northeast China shall be executed by the Ministry of Finance ordering the Inspector General of Customs. It will be announced on the 24th and implemented starting on October 1st. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs will notify the League of Nations and issue a public statement to all countries explaining the inability of the Northeast China customs to perform their duties and the reasons for relocating tax collection, to facilitate understanding. As for the relocated tax collection measures, goods transported from various locations to Northeast China will have the taxes of the destination collected at the first customs point of export. Goods transported out of Northeast China will have the taxes of the place of origin collected at the first customs point after entry. Qin Fen, Acting Superintendent of Customs, went to Shanghai on the evening of the 23rd to meet with Minister Song to report on the Executive Yuan's resolution and to confer with Inspector General of Customs Frederick Maze to prepare for the implementation of various measures. (Special dispatch, 23rd)

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Transportation, due to the seizure of customs houses in Northeast China by puppet organizations, will, starting on the 25th, require all commercial ships to pay tonnage dues upon entry, otherwise ship licenses will be refused and passage prohibited. It has decided to formulate countermeasures to deal with this and is currently planning comprehensively. (Special dispatch, 23rd)

Key Points of Regulations on Collection of Tax on Paper Currency Issuance

(Nanjing) The key points of the paper currency issuance tax rate and collection regulations passed by the Executive Yuan meeting are as follows: 1. Banks specially licensed to issue convertible banknotes must pay a convertible banknote issuance tax; 2. Banks issuing convertible banknotes must have a 100% reserve, with 60% as cash reserve and 40% as guarantee reserve; 3. The tax rate is based on the amount of the guarantee reserve, originally set at 2.5%, now amended to 1.25%. The cash reserve portion is exempt from issuance tax; 4. The issuance tax is collected annually, at the beginning of each year; 5. If the Ministry of Finance deems the number declared by a bank to be inaccurate, it may temporarily organize a review committee to assess it. The review committee is composed of one representative each from the Ministry of Finance, the Ministry of Audit, the Bankers Association, and the Chamber of Commerce; 6. If a bank fails to pay the convertible banknote issuance tax, the Ministry of Finance may revoke its special issuance right. The above regulations will be submitted to the Legislative Yuan for deliberation and implementation after approval. (Special dispatch, 23rd)

Remnants of Bandits in Honghu Can Be Cleared Up Within Days

(Hankou) He Chengjun was scheduled to fly to Hankou from Tianmen on the 23rd but changed his departure to the afternoon of the 24th. Xu Yuanquan, after meeting with Zhu Huaibing in Fengkou, returned to Zhuhe, and will return to Xinti on the 23rd. After He returns, he will also come to Hankou for a trip. The remnants of the bandits in Honghu can be cleared up by the 25th after being surrounded and suppressed. Jiang telegraphed Zhang Zhenhan, expressing deep appreciation. (Special dispatch, 23rd)

(Hankou) The Yong Sui, Min Sheng, Min Quan, Xian Ning, De Sheng, Wei Sheng, Shun Sheng, Gong Sheng, Yi Sheng, Ren Sheng, and other ships of the Second Fleet of the Navy have made meritorious contributions in suppressing bandits in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River. (Hankou) On the 21st, Luo Qijiang's troops attacked the Xiaogu two divisions entrenched in Huiwang Mountain and Bijia Mountain on the border of Henan and Hubei. Xinji and Jinjiazhai Decided to Be Re-established as Two Counties

Proposed Names Are Jingfu and Lihuang

To Commemorate the Merits of Ji Liuwei

And to Immediately Implement the Military Reclamation System

(Hankou) Jiang has decided to re-establish Xinji and Jinjiazhai as two counties, both under Henan Province. Originally, it was proposed to name them Yongjing and Yongning, but to commemorate the merits of Ji Ying, Liu Zhi, and Wei Lihuang, it was decided to rename Xinji as Jingfu County and Jinjiazhai as Lihuang County. It is reported that Liu Zhi has already recommended two county magistrates, with the treatment of administrative commissioners. Also, Jiang stipulated that in the bandit suppression area, any county where the area of barren land exceeds six-tenths of the total cultivated land area of the county will be designated as a military reclamation county. All the barren land in the military reclamation county will be nationalized, and land will be allocated to active-duty soldiers for cultivation, with each soldier receiving approximately three to seven mu of land. All the regulations

are extremely detailed. Regarding the military reclamation measures, Jingfu and Lihuang counties will be the first to pilot them. This military reclamation system is the military-agricultural policy established by Jiang. (Special dispatch, 23rd)

(Hankou) Liu Zhi previously telegraphed Jiang, requesting disaster relief for the newly recovered bandit areas in Henan. Jiang replied, saying that the disaster situation was grievous and inquired about measures to provide disaster relief to the affected people and to revive the rural villages, as well as the amount of disaster relief materials needed, and promised to do his best to remedy the situation. (Special dispatch, 23rd)

(Nanjing) According to military sources, after the recapture of Jinjiazhai, the remnants of the bandits fled in confusion towards the areas of Lu'an and Huoshan. Important Telegrams Three

Kidnapping of Two British Nationals in Niuzhuang

(Shenyang) The location of Mrs. Bowler and Mr. Kirkland has been learned today. A farmer in a certain village saw them. It is said that the two are currently living in a thatched cottage in a certain village 30 miles east of Panshan, away from Niuzhuang, guarded by a number of bandits. They are treated well. The farmer spoke with the bandit leader, who said that the bandits would not harm the two, but they are currently short of food. (Reuters dispatch, 23rd)

Niuzhuang A horseman surnamed Wang, who is an intermediary in contact with the bandits, claimed today that he, Mrs. Bowler, and Mr. Kirkland were kidnapped together, but detained separately. On September 21, the bandits blindfolded him, and after passing through tall sorghum stalks for a long distance, they released him to return, to prevent him from recognizing the direction. The bandits number about 300 and are gathered near Baiguoshu, ten miles north of Yingkou. They ordered him to tell the relatives of the kidnapped to send the ransom quickly. (Reuters dispatch, 23rd)

Niuzhuang It was learned today that when Mrs. Bowler was kidnapped, her two dogs were also not spared. One dog was an Alsatian and the other an Irish setter. Yesterday, the large Alsatian dog suddenly escaped from the bandit den and found its way back to Niuzhuang. When it arrived in front of Doctor Philip's residence, it barked wildly, seemingly indicating that its mistress was still alive not far from Niuzhuang. The two dogs seemed to have agreed that one would bring news back while the other stayed with the mistress. According to a Chinese servant who returned to Niuzhuang today, the small Irish setter never leaves its mistress, sleeping by her side at night and eating the leftovers in her bowl. Although the bandits repeatedly chased it away, it would not leave her side. (Reuters dispatch, 23rd)

(London) The parents of Mr. Kirkland, the British national kidnapped in Niuzhuang, received a recent Reuters telegram from Shenyang, learned of their son's location, and that the bandits are treating him very well, which greatly relieved them. Mrs. Kirkland believes that this news is definitely optimistic, and said that she met a person who was kidnapped by Chinese bandits for three weeks, and was later released because the bandits became tired of him. (Reuters dispatch, 23rd)

Niuzhuang The bandit leader is currently demanding 600,000 yuan in cash, two machine guns, and 500,000 rounds of ammunition as ransom for Mr. Kirkland. As for Mrs. Bowler, a huge amount of cash is required. The horseman was not tied after being kidnapped and had many opportunities to escape, but because he has known Mrs. Bowler since childhood, he could not bear to leave her. The rumor that Mrs. Bowler rode a donkey through the village is not true. She was forced to walk everywhere. (Reuters dispatch, 23rd)

Niuzhuang Doctor Philip's Chinese servant brought a new letter from the bandits, so there is more hope of rescuing the two. The bandit letter reiterates the previous demands, states that they are both safe and healthy, and are being treated well. (Reuters dispatch, 23rd)

Foreign Important Telegrams

League of Nations Administrative Council Opens Yesterday

Free State Executive President Fan Lela Presides

Passes China's Education Investigation Report

Sino-Japanese Dispute May Not Be Brought Up for Discussion

Tune in to Wireless Broadcasts Every Week Starting Tomorrow

▲ Reuters, Geneva, 23rd: The League of Nations Administrative Council held a closed meeting at 11:10 AM today, lasting about half an hour. This was followed by a public meeting. During the closed meeting, Yan Huiqing, the Chief Representative of China, inquired why China's petition to the League of Nations regarding Japanese aggression was listed as the final item on the agenda. Yan also emphatically stated that this matter should be discussed urgently. The Chairman informed Yan that the Lytton Commission's report was not yet complete and that Japan had requested a six-week delay in the discussion after the report was published. This matter will be considered by the Administrative Council.

▲ Guomin Agency, Geneva, 23rd: The League of Nations Council convened this morning at 11:00 AM, presided over by Fan Lela, Executive President of the Irish Free State. It is currently believed here that while the Sino-Japanese dispute is listed at the end of the agenda, it may not be discussed at this session of the Council. Japan seems to have no intention of engaging in a verbal battle within the Council regarding the League of Nations investigation report but is preparing to respond in the League of Nations General Assembly. It is now expected that the investigation team's report will first be discussed by the new Council after the election and then handed over to the special session of the League of Nations General Assembly to be convened in November.

▲ Reuters, London, 23rd: The Huimin Pao's Geneva correspondent reports that the (Manchukuo)'s document to the League of Nations cannot be distributed to the members of the League of Nations because in the eyes of the League of Nations, (Manchukuo) is not a real country. The correspondent suggests that (Manchukuo), under Japanese guidance, should apply to join the League of Nations. Furthermore, the League of Nations' response will undoubtedly be the final and absolute touchstone for (Manchukuo)'s demand for independent sovereignty.

▲ Reuters, Geneva, 23rd: The Administrative Council today formed a committee with three members to find a solution to the dispute between Bolivia and Paraguay.

▲ Reuters, Geneva, 23rd: A report to the Administrative Council mentioned the work of the League of Nations Educational Investigation Team in China. The report was passed unanimously. Dr. Yan Huiqing stated that the Chinese government was extremely satisfied with the work accomplished by the investigation team under very difficult circumstances. Although he could not fully agree with all the points made by the team, the members of the investigation team were truly worthy of the highest praise. He believed that the fusion of Eastern and Western educational ideas would surely achieve excellent results.

▲ Reuters, Geneva, 23rd: At today's meeting of the Administrative Council, Norwegian representative Han Bailuo stated that many member states have not paid their dues and that if this is not remedied promptly, there is concern that the League will face financial difficulties next year.

▲ Guomin Agency, Geneva, 22nd: Starting from the 25th, every Sunday morning, the League of Nations' two radio stations will broadcast in English, French, and Spanish between 11:00 and 11:45 (Shanghai time 6:20 to 7:05 AM) on the work of the League of Nations. The wavelengths will be 40.3 and 20.62 meters. The first broadcast will be addressed by Secretary-General Drummond.

British League of Nations Association Studies Stance on Japan

Better to Withdraw Than Have No Determination to Abide by Covenants

Territorial Changes Not to be Recognized if There is Opposition

▲ Havas, London, 23rd: The Executive Committee of the British League of Nations Association, chaired by Lord Cecil, has conducted a lengthy study of the stance on Japan. The conclusion reached is that it is better for member states of the League of Nations to withdraw from the League than to have no determination to abide by the obligations of the covenant. This conclusion is based on the speeches of Briand and Simon, who stated that any country that is infringed upon and seeks redress can only use peaceful methods and has no right to use other means. The Executive Committee's conclusion also cited moral principles, stating that if a country invades another country and changes its territory, this change should not be recognized if there is opposition from one party.

Japanese Army Minister Araki Sadao Observes the Situation

Says Japan Will Never Withdraw From the League of Nations

▲ Dentsu, Tokyo, 23rd: Army Minister Araki met with German journalist Zihilin and Dutch journalist Linde at his official residence yesterday afternoon and replied to the two journalists' questions about the rumors of Japan's withdrawal from the League of Nations, saying that Japan, which considers world peace, would never leave the League of Nations. Since the establishment of the League of Nations, Japan has faithfully worked for the League of Nations, but the League of Nations' response to Japan has been 13 to 1, which is inevitably too harsh. Therefore, if the League of Nations does not understand Japan's position, forcing Japan to withdraw, or hoping that Japan will withdraw, that is another matter.

Creating Atmosphere in the United States Has Another Purpose

▲ Hualian News Agency, Tokyo, 23rd: The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs recently secretly ordered Saito Hiroshi, the acting ambassador to the United States, to create an atmosphere of withdrawal from the League of Nations in the United States. It is reported that Acting Ambassador Saito hosted a group of news reporters in Washington yesterday and said that if the report is unfavorable to Japan, Japan will undoubtedly take the decision to withdraw from the League of Nations. Regarding Saito's remarks, according to investigations, he has secretly contacted presidential candidate Roosevelt to create a threatening atmosphere with an attitude that disregards everything, attempting to restrain Hoover and instigate American pacifists to oppose Stimson.

International Situation Changes

Russo-Japanese Amity and Franco-American Cooperation

Have Become the Focus of Discussion in Parisian Political Circles

▲ Guomin Agency, Paris, 22nd: The theory of Russo-Japanese amity has become the focus of discussion in political circles here. According to the Morning Post's Washington correspondent, Russia and Japan are currently conducting negotiations, with Japan intending to purchase Russian oil and no longer rely on American supply. Japanese businessman Matsuoka is stationed in Moscow to handle these negotiations. Since the United States decided to concentrate the majority of its fleet in Pearl Harbor in the Hawaiian Islands, Japan has become increasingly wary and is therefore eager for the success of the negotiations. The success or failure of the Russo-Japanese oil agreement depends on two conditions: (1) improving the convenience of oil transportation, and (2) a compromise between the two governments regarding (Manchukuo). The correspondent also stated that Japan is prepared to allow Soviet Russian goods to be transported into Manchuria with preferential tariff rights in exchange for its recognition of (Manchukuo) and is willing to guarantee the Soviet Russian interests in the China Eastern Railway. At the same time, political circles here are also eagerly discussing the British newspaper reports that France has changed its Far Eastern policy and is seeking friendship with the United States. According to this news, US Senator Reed had lengthy talks with French Prime Minister Herriot and other politicians, suggesting that if France could support the United States' Far Eastern policy, the United States would be willing to help France deal with Germany's demands for military equality. French newspapers have remained silent on this news to date, but diplomatic circles generally believe it to be true, although these negotiations cannot yet be said to have concluded.

▲ Guomin Agency, Moscow, 23rd: The Associated Press has learned from usually reliable sources that Soviet Russia has agreed to accept consuls and attendants sent by the Manchukuo puppet organization, allowing them to reside in Blagoveshchensk, Vladivostok, Khabarovsk, and other Far Eastern ports. Passports for the puppet consul in Blagoveshchensk have already been signed.

British Conservative Party Inclines Toward Friendliness with Japan

But Autonomous Regions Unanimously Advocate Alliance with the United States

▲ Guomin Agency, Washington, 22nd: The previous report that US Senator Reed went to Europe under the orders of the State Department to explore the Far Eastern policies of Britain and France has been confirmed today. Reed is scheduled to return to Washington before the release of the League of Nations investigation report. It is reported that the British autonomous regions are advising London to support the League of Nations and support the United States, but a powerful group of conservatives within Britain opposes taking any path that could jeopardize British-Japanese relations. France's attitude is that it is prepared to support the League of Nations because if the League of Nations cannot handle the Northeast crisis, its influence in Europe will be greatly diminished, which is of extreme concern to France.

US Army Chief of Staff's Tour of Europe Has Significant Meaning

Purpose Is to Investigate the Military Preparations of Russia's Neighbors

To Make Preparations for Future Far Eastern Warfare

▲ Guomin Agency, Vienna, 23rd: US Army Chief of Staff General MacWalter is currently touring Europe and has arrived in Romania as a guest of the Romanian King. The capitals of Eastern European countries are still commenting on the General's tour of Europe. Political circles here now believe that the General has a mission to investigate the military preparations of the countries bordering the Soviet Union. This is not only related to the Geneva Disarmament Conference, but it is also said to be for the sake of an eventual war between Russia and Japan. Disarmament Conference Faces Many Hidden Reefs

Russian Representative Demands Political Discussions Be Held Earlier

Britain and France Oppose, Causing Tense Atmosphere at the Conference

Steering Committee Adjourns Until Next Tuesday

Germany Does Not Participate in Extraneous Consultations on the Issue

▲ Guomin Agency, Geneva, 22nd: The tense atmosphere within the Disarmament Conference Steering Committee erupted this afternoon, and considering the future, the disturbances will not end. This was because the Russian representative Litvinov ignited the fuse, almost causing the committee to openly break down, and finally adjourned until next Tuesday to save the situation. When they gathered this morning, Litvinov ridiculed the proposal to discuss the organization and management of the Arms Committee in extremely frank and profound terms while the disarmament process had not yet been determined. When the meeting continued in the afternoon, Litvinov continued to attack, demanding that the conference discuss from a political point of view again, insisting that it would be useless to discuss the second step before the first step problem had been agreed upon. British Foreign Minister Simon, with the support of French Minister Longchamp, strongly debated, claiming that the committee must abide by the agenda. Finally, Chairman Henderson expressed his opinion, declaring that the Steering Committee should only abide by the rules of the meeting and not restrict the scope of debate. However, it is advisable to first contact privately on the German issue. Judging from the final development of the meeting, it increasingly gives the impression that the Disarmament Conference has encountered reefs and must make great efforts to get out of the reefs. That is to say, the adjournment of the Steering Committee this time, although opposed by the French, already has the appearance of an indefinite extension. As for the German delegation, it has repeatedly stated that Germany is determined not to join the discussion until its demands for equality are recognized, and indicated that the German Foreign Minister intends not to reply to Henderson's letter for the time being, but wants to contact Henderson privately. The time of their meeting may be before or after the meeting between Nereis and Simon tonight.

British Leasehold Issue

Britain Raises Friendly Negotiations with Japan

▲ Dentsu, Tokyo, 23rd: British Ambassador to Japan Sir Lindley visited Foreign Minister Uchida yesterday afternoon and presented a fundamental solution private plan regarding the Yokohama and Kobe trading port area permanent leasehold issue, which has been unresolved for many years since the Meiji era, hoping to start formal negotiations based on this. Public Telegram

Telegram from Huangchuan: All newspaper offices are hereby informed that bandits have been disturbing southern Henan for several years, occupying the areas of Shangcheng, Guangshan, Gushi, Luoshan, and the fifth and sixth districts of Huangchuan for the longest time. As I, Zhang Fang, have personally experienced many places and have more detailed knowledge, the bandit areas have been completely emptied of people, livestock, and belongings. Fields and ditches have been almost completely destroyed. For hundreds of miles, smoke from cooking fires has ceased and no chickens or dogs remain. A scene of desolation is unbearable to witness. Even the remaining ears of grain are scattered. Now that the bandit gangs have fled far away, the area has been restored, and news of the victory has spread, the people have all come here. However, the houses are ruined, and the fields are barren. Eradicating the weeds and repairing the damage is urgent. However, there are no tools or draft cattle, and there is nothing to trade to purchase them. Therefore, those who linger in the wide market, weeping at the doors, are everywhere. At dusk, when their paths are exhausted, sadness comes from within. Some say they must die, and some say it is difficult to live. The old and weak cry and plead, which is heartbreaking to hear. I have investigated the areas of Shangcheng, Guangshan, Gushi, Luoshan, and the fifth and sixth districts of Huangchuan, which are mountainous and picturesque, and used to be rich and fertile areas. Now, the dilapidated walls and ruins have become dens for foxes and rabbits. At this time when the old crops are exhausted and the new crops have not yet come in, it is not possible to appease and gather the people and recruit and appease the refugees unless the government, philanthropists, or charitable organizations provide assistance and give them the means to maintain the current situation and gradually seek the future, so as to avoid the good fields from turning into dense grass and millions of lives from being filled in ditches. The Mid-Autumn Festival has passed, and it is time to sow seeds. Next year, there is still hope for a wheat harvest. Otherwise, once the farming season is over, recovery will be even more difficult. What I have investigated, I respectfully ask on behalf of millions of helpless people, I beseech you to provide relief, and earnestly request you to quickly grant your full support, allocate grain and funds, and distribute them, bestowing blessings on the people. The merit and virtue of this will be immeasurable. The telegram is urgent, and I cannot express my prayers enough. Zhang Fang kowtows and begs for consideration.

Important News

The Japanese Military's Manchurian Construction Fantasies

▲ Development Plans Published in Japanese Newspapers Mostly Written by Military Personnel

▲ Plans for Colonization, Transportation, and Military Affairs Are Extremely Ruthless

▲ Foreigners Wonder Whether Such Imaginations Exceed Fantasy

The *North-China Daily News*'s September 17th Tokyo dispatch states: "Japan has now formally recognized 'Manchukuo.' Newspapers and magazines are filled with articles on the colony's exploitation and development plans, and many are penned by military personnel. While these cannot be regarded as representing the government's will, it must be understood that today's Japanese military can control everything, especially regarding measures concerning 'Manchukuo' and China. Therefore, the opinions expressed in these articles should not be taken lightly. Moreover, the structure and tone of these articles are largely the same; discerning observers know they originate from a single source. Each article begins by stating that Japan's 'great' mission in the Asian continent is partially completed. From now on, the Japanese should focus on developing and securing the fruits obtained by 'our country's warriors sacrificing their lives.' As for the administration of 'Manchukuo,' the articles advocate that the new government, for the sake of convenience, might as well be a Chinese government—that is, composed of Manchus and Chinese. However, one crucial point is that the new government's administrative power and financial integrity must not be impaired in the slightest. In other words, their intention is to imply that the government established by the Japanese military when thirty million 'Manchurians' declared independence, yearning for self-determination, is ultimately untrustworthy. The articles state that Japan, to ensure the government's power and financial integrity, has constructed a 'steel system' managed by Japanese, and has established an internal government overseen by Japanese officials within the 'Manchukuo' government to control its policies. This is merely a small wheel within a larger wheel of ostensible 'autonomy.' Japan is now striving to make the 'Manchukuo' government consistently pro-Japanese. The articles claim that if 'Manchukuo' is not pro-Japanese, if old conspirators and resistors show signs of raising their heads, and if things quickly revert to the old ways, then annexation would be unavoidable. As for colonization, the articles state that the living standards of Japanese farmers and workers are certainly higher than those of Chinese, Manchus, and Koreans. However, farmers in northern and northeastern Japan are now in dire straits, nearly starving. Their current situation is far inferior to opening up the lands in 'Manchukuo.' Therefore, the major obstacle to relocating farmers from Hokkaido to 'Manchukuo' has been largely eliminated. Furthermore, a special zone twelve miles wide will be designated on both sides of the main railways for Japanese immigrants to reside in. Within these zones, doctors, teachers, ironworkers, carpenters, priests, etc., will be stationed. High walls with loopholes for rifles and machine guns will be built around each village. Every household will be given weapons, and all men will be required to undergo regular military training. Residents will swear to serve in the military in times of emergency. The cost of weaponry and the construction of fortresses around each village will be allocated by the central government. The properties of former administrators and their followers will be confiscated, but not distributed to the 'Manchukuo' residents, but to Japanese immigrants. Restrictions will be placed on Chinese immigrants. These model new villages will initially be populated by Koreans, with Japanese village chiefs and mayors appointed. In addition, railway construction can provide employment for Japanese workers and greatly benefit the Japanese steel industry. The northern section of the Huai-Tun Railway is particularly important. It can directly transport products from northern Manchuria to the ice-free ports of the Korean coast and provide an essential transportation route for troops in the event of war with Russia. The Japanese often say that Japan should regard the Hinggan Mountains as its first line of defense on the mainland. Now that this new road is nearing completion, Japan can have a completely self-managed new road directly connecting to northern Manchuria, which is essential for troop movements. Anyone studying the structure of the new 'Manchukuo' government should note the conspicuous absence of a Ministry of Education. It is said that the new country does not want 'black-shirted' youths. The articles also state that the western border of 'Manchukuo' (i.e., bordering mainland China) has not yet been defined. It is hoped that 'Manchukuo' can enable its residents to live and work in peace and become a paradise, so that provinces of mainland China, such as Hebei and Shanxi, will voluntarily return. The articles do not mention Rehe, implying that the Rehe province will sooner or later be annexed into 'Manchukuo.' The articles also mention that 'Manchukuo' will not be able to defend itself against China or Soviet Russia in the future, so Japan should assume the responsibility of protecting 'Manchukuo.' Japan also plans to organize security forces composed of Manchus, Han Chinese, Japanese, Koreans, and Mongols within 'Manchukuo' to protect internal security. The training officers will be Japanese, which will be the prototype of the 'Manchukuo' army in the future, with plans to train 80,000 people in the first step. According to all the above, these are all plans for Japan to develop and exploit 'Manchukuo.' Many readers are surprised, wondering if such imaginations exceed fantasy. They contain great difficulties and will hinder Japan's internal politics and social organization and its external relations. However, the military will never lightly stop what they have already started. Their attitude is just as the New Testament says: "No one who puts his hand to the plow and looks back is fit for service in the kingdom of God."

The Masses in Jiaodong Rise Up Against Liu

▲ Liu's Troops Suffer Repeated Defeats and Retreat to Huang County to Defend

Qingdao Dispatch: After the armies of Han and Liu made contact, Liu's troops, to preserve their strength, did not resist Han's troops with all their might and retreated. Therefore, Han's troops made steady progress and occupied Pingdu and Yexian one after another in just two days. However, in the battle of Shentangzhen on the 19th, fierce fighting occurred between the two sides, and both armies suffered some casualties. Liu's troops then retreated to defend Yexian. Later, because Han's plainclothes soldiers had long been lying in ambush in the city, when Han's troops arrived, the plainclothes soldiers responded from within. Liu's troops abandoned the city and concentrated in Zhuqiaozhen to await reinforcements. The vanguard of Han's troops arrived yesterday morning (the 20th) at a place twenty miles from Zhuqiao and began to deploy for the attack and immediately launched an offensive. It is reported that Liu's troops have been shaken by repeated defeats, and Zhuqiao has no natural defenses to defend, so they plan to abandon Zhuqiao and retreat to Huang County to defend. Currently, from Longkou in the north to Beimazhaoyuantou in the south, trenches have been dug everywhere in preparation for resistance. Liu's reinforcements have been transported to the front line as much as possible, so a large army has gathered in the Longkou area, and the people's grain has been requisitioned, causing panic among the residents. A major battle is imminent. Liu's troops have also levied huge sums from various counties in the name of raising military funds. The two small counties of Wendeng and Rongcheng have been allocated as much as 250,000 yuan each. It can be inferred from this the amount levied on other counties. The militia and civil defense forces in various counties, unable to bear the harassment, have united and risen up against Liu, and have also sent telegrams to various parties requesting assistance. The text of the telegram is as follows: I, Liu Zhennian, the commander of the 21st Division of the Army, was originally the chief of staff of Fang Yongchang's army under the former Zhili-Shandong Allied Army. With the heart of a jackal and an unbridled nature, when Zhang Zongchang failed, he took advantage of the opportunity to instigate the troops to turn against Fang Yongchang and defected to the Revolutionary Army, still stationed in the Yantai and Penglai areas of Jiaodong, expanding his power and usurping political power. In the past, the Central Government repeatedly dispatched the division to set out for battle, but the commander of the division made many excuses and did not leave the defense area. His intention was to monopolize Jiaodong and permanently maintain his position. Therefore, the heads of the various counties and other officials within the division's defense zone are all appointed by the division commander, and the provincial government cannot intervene. All grain taxes and other funds in the various counties are levied and extorted by the division commander, not collected in accordance with the regulations of the Central Government, and each county is additionally levied a monthly military supply fee of 80,000 to 120,000 yuan. It is estimated that each county collects at least 2 million yuan per year. The division occupies more than a dozen counties, and a total of more than 24 million yuan of military expenses are collected each year, which is truly shocking. Although there are occasional cases where the people of the various counties, unable to bear the extortion, rise up to resist, the commander of the division adds the crime of counter-revolution or the crime of plotting against the Red Spear Society, and arbitrarily slaughters them. Therefore, the people dare not disobey any longer. The division commander covers the sky with one hand, forcing the people's organizations to distribute telegrams of praise and virtue, and establishing newspapers to publicize his merits. Therefore, the weak people under the slaughter submit and obey, listening to his arbitrary exploitation. Jiaodong is a rich and abundant area of Shandong Province, with grain reserves in every family and savings in every household. After being exploited by Liu Zhennian for five years, the fat has been exhausted and the blood has been drained. Many middle and lower-class households have abandoned their properties and fled, and even the upper-class households have been forced to abandon their homes and seek refuge. They have repeatedly pleaded with the Central Government and the provincial government for rescue, but they have been ignored. Millions of people cannot ask for death and cannot survive. The rich area has become a desolate market, and the prosperous merchants and farmers have become fish in a dried-up ditch. It is truly a strange calamity unprecedented in ancient times. The people have no way to call for help, and their wealth is exhausted. They have no choice but to unite and hand their heads over to the vicious and evil Liu Zhennian, preferring to be ghosts who die by bullets rather than souls who starve to death. Seeking life in death, there may be a glimmer of hope. In addition to risking our lives with Liu Zhennian, we respectfully submit a tearful appeal, begging for assistance. This is our utmost hope. In tears, the representatives of millions of refugees in the thirteen counties of Jiaodong, Li Lizhou and others, kowtow together. (21st)

On the Eve of the September 18th Incident in Fuzhou

▲ The 19th Route Army Pastes Anti-Japanese Slogans Everywhere

▲ Taiwanese Cigarette Seller Fang Shengtau Actually Yields

Fuzhou Dispatch: For the first anniversary of the September 18th National Humiliation Day, the Fujian Provincial Party Headquarters and the 19th Route Army originally planned to hold a mass rally at the public stadium and organize propaganda teams to go to the countryside to give speeches, in order to arouse the people's spirit. However, because the provincial government did not agree due to the serious diplomatic situation, the provincial party headquarters temporarily changed the meeting to a representative assembly of all circles in the headquarters auditorium. The 19th Route Army still convened its officers and soldiers from the First Supplementary Brigade to hold a meeting at the public stadium on its own. The public who wanted to participate were also welcome. At the same time, the various regiments and battalions of the brigade posted slogans throughout the city, such as "Swear to Avenge the National Humiliation," "Recover the Lost Territories," and "Implement Economic Boycott." For more than eight months, no anti-Japanese slogans had been seen in Fuzhou society (the anti-Japanese slogans posted previously were washed away by the provincial government in early January of this year due to protests from the Japanese consulate). Suddenly seeing them again, the atmosphere became tense. On the morning of the 17th, the masses in the Xiadu area, because a certain Mr. Jia, a native of Fuqing County, rented a foreign license from a Taiwanese to open a smoking den, with lights on inside and people gathering to smoke, and selling Haelian fish, banana fruit and Lu outside, with smokers coming and going all night long, and fighting and disturbing the neighborhood late at night, negotiated with him, but the Fuqing man held the power of the foreign license and was unreasonable, arousing public anger. The masses only poured the Haelian fish, banana fruit, and Lu arranged in front of the store into the center of the street. The Fuqing man went to report to the Taiwanese, who reported to the Japanese consulate. The Japanese consul, Mr. Moriya, immediately protested to the provincial government, saying that the Chinese had gathered to destroy a Japanese merchant's foreign firm in memory of September 18, causing losses of more than 7,000 yuan. If the Chinese government had no solution, he would send marines ashore to stand guard and protect the area around Cangqianshan Fanchuanpu. His words were extremely stern. Residents around Qiaonan were greatly alarmed upon hearing the news. Tan Qixiu, the brigade commander of the Supplementary Brigade of the 19th Route Army, upon receiving the report, immediately dispatched armed troops in the afternoon to set up posts around Cangqianshan Fanchuanpu to protect the area and announced martial law. Fang Shengtau, the acting chairman of the provincial government, upon hearing that the 19th Route Army had gone to Qiaonan, fearing a conflict with the Japanese marines, immediately acknowledged the Japanese consul's request, compensated 7,000 yuan, and asked the Japanese marines not to land. On the evening of the 17th, another report was received, saying that the Japanese would gather more than 200 Japanese and Taiwanese ruffians to provoke trouble when the Chinese held meetings and parades. On the morning of the 18th, Brigade Commander Tan again sent troops to set up posts in various important places, and the Public Security Bureau also ordered the entire security team to go out on patrol. At 11:00, the National Humiliation Day Commemoration Meeting opened at the stadium, with more than 2,000 soldiers and more than 1,000 civilians attending. Tan Qixiu served as chairman, and his speech was extremely impassioned. After the meeting, at about 1:00 in the afternoon, a parade set out. The civilians were in the center, and the soldiers were on both sides. The soldiers and civilians shouted slogans along the way, circling the city for a week before returning to the stadium to dismiss the team. The troops did not withdraw their sentries and lift martial law until the evening. (September 19)

The Aftermath of the Bandit Areas in Western Anhui Is Underway

▲ Jinjiazhai Is Being Changed to a County Seat and Will Be Implemented

▲ The Provincial Government Sends Personnel to Accompany Various Armies in Handling the Aftermath

▲ The Department of Finance Formulates Measures to Reduce and Exempt Land Taxes

Anqing Correspondence: The bandit atmosphere in Anhui Province has recently gradually subsided. Jinjiazhai, which belongs to Liu'an County, has long been occupied by bandits as a nest. Now, according to a telegram from Hankou, the provincial government has learned that Wei Lihuang's troops recovered Jinjiazhai on the 20th and captured countless bandits. The 33rd Brigade was ordered to pay attention to blocking and attacking the scattered bandits, and the chief magistrate of Liu'an and the committee members accompanying the army to handle the aftermath were ordered to properly prepare for the local aftermath. The change of Jinjiazhai to a county seat has been rumored for a long time. Recently, Commander-in-Chief Chiang also plans to establish a county in the area, naming it Xinning, under the jurisdiction of Anhui. Now that it has been recovered, its realization should not be far away. In addition, Yingshan in Anhui has suffered from bandit disasters for a long time. Recently, it was ordered by Chiang via telegram to be transferred to the jurisdiction of the Third Administrative Region of Hubei. The provincial government has submitted this to the previous Standing Committee for resolution and compliance, and

Page 12

has consulted with the Hubei Provincial Government to determine the date of transfer. These are all important measures for the aftermath in western Anhui. However, the provincial government previously appointed Tang Qiyao as the special commissioner for the aftermath of the seven counties of western Anhui, namely Liu'an, Yingshan, Huoshan, Huoqiu, Shouxian, Shucheng, and Hefei, which had been repeatedly ravaged by bandits. Recently, Tang resigned due to illness, and the provincial government changed the appointment to Wang Zhuren, the chief magistrate of Hefei, to concurrently serve as the acting commissioner. All facilities in the bandit areas can be gradually implemented, and Provincial Councilor Zhang Haizhou was sent to Wang Jun's troops, Provincial Councilor Jiang Yi was sent to Xu Tingyao's troops, and Provincial Councilor Tang Guangji was sent to Liang Guanying's troops to serve as committee members accompanying the army to handle the aftermath. They have already departed separately. In addition, the provincial government, in accordance with the telegram order from the Henan-Hubei-Anhui Bandit Suppression Headquarters to investigate and verify the regular and additional taxes in the bandit-stricken areas and exempt them separately, forwarded the order to the Department of Finance for compliance. The Department of Finance has now formulated measures to reduce and exempt regular and additional taxes, dividing them into four categories: full exemption, reduction and exemption, discretionary levy, and deferred levy. The Liu'an Chief County Government was first ordered to conduct a detailed investigation in the villages and fortresses of Yingshan, Huoshan, and other counties, report the results for verification, and then submit a report to the provincial government for forwarding to the headquarters. (September 23)

The Ministry of Interior Announces Measures to Prohibit Slavery and the Keeping of Maids

The Ministry of Interior previously considered that slavery and the keeping of maids were inhumane and drafted measures to prohibit them, and submitted them to the Executive Yuan for review and approval. The case has now been approved by the Executive Yuan's directive, and the Ministry yesterday specifically announced it with a ministry order, the full text of which is as follows: (1) All slaves and maids who are not in an employment relationship, regardless of whether they are kept through buying, selling, gifting, or charitable relations, are prohibited in accordance with these measures. (2) The steps to prohibit slavery and the keeping of maids are as follows: 1. Persuasion; 2. Liberation; 3. Relief; 4. Punishment. The preceding steps shall be handled separately in accordance with the following articles. (3) Each directly subordinate municipal government and each city and county government subordinate to the province shall supervise the police organs to conduct thorough investigations. If any slavery or maid-keeping is discovered, the relevant city and county government must be immediately reported and persuasion implemented. In the capital or public security bureaus directly subordinate to the province, it may be directly executed by the respective police organs. (4) Those who keep slaves and maids must, after being persuaded, liberate their keeping relationship within a certain period. If they wish to continue using them, they should all be changed to employment, and wages should be given appropriately. The employed and the employer both have the freedom to terminate the employment relationship at any time. (5) If each city and county liberates a large number of slaves and maids at the same time, and the employment relationship cannot be established for a while, the following methods shall be used for relief: (1) Unmarried slaves and maids who have a home

to return to should be sent home. If there is no home to return to, or if the family is unable to support them and is unwilling to take them in, they should be sent to the local relief center for adoption. If there is no relief center, the local government shall find ways to send them to charitable organizations for nurturing. (2) Slaves and maids who have reached adulthood, regardless of gender, must be allowed to choose their own spouses and find other jobs. If there is no suitable spouse for a while and there is a danger of unemployment and starvation, the local government may appropriately send them to a relief center or charitable organization for placement. (6) Those who keep slaves and maids, after being persuaded and given a deadline to liberate them, still fail to comply, or newly keep them after the announcement of these measures, the city and county governments shall, in addition to sending them to the judicial organs for handling in accordance with Article 313 of the Criminal Law for the crime of enslaving people, and immediately forcibly liberating the slaves and maids they are keeping.

, and may also impose a fine of up to 300 yuan, which shall be used by the local relief center or other charitable organization to relieve unemployed slaves and maids. (7) The city and county governments subordinate to each provincial government and the directly subordinate public security bureaus shall, within three months of receiving these measures, submit the handling situation to the provincial government for forwarding to the Ministry of Interior for verification. The handling situation of the directly subordinate municipal governments and the capital police department shall be directly reported to the Ministry of Interior for verification. (8) These measures shall be implemented from the date of approval and promulgation.

Journey to the West (20) (IV)

Extending Amidst Eight Scenic Spots

On August 1st, in addition to inspecting the oil factory, we also investigated various local conditions. We learned that the entire county of Yanchang has a population of 21,000 people, with more than 3,600 households, and an area of approximately 4,500 acres. The city walls were built on high mountains, seemingly paying considerable attention to the defense against bandits. The only street with a market is a main road. Commerce is bleak, and the scene is desolate. Residents all express that taxes are too heavy and that it is almost impossible to make a living. Almost the entire county is mountainous, with very little flat land. The flat land along both sides of the Yan River and at the top of the mountains is slightly fertile and can be used to grow cotton and wheat. The flat land at the top of the mountains can yield two dou of wheat per mu (each dou is 50 catties), and the hillside land can yield one dou. In terms of the entire county, the land planted with cotton accounts for about one-tenth, cultivated land accounts for seven-tenths, and wasteland accounts for three-tenths. The annual land tax is about 6,000 yuan. In addition, there are miscellaneous taxes or surcharges. On average, each person can cultivate about 30 mu of land.

In terms of scenery, there is Phoenix Ridge 30 li west of the city, and Yongyi Bridge near the south of the city, which is said to be a naturally formed bridge. Originally, there were six arches, but now there are only two. Near the east of the city is Suyu Spring, where the water is fragrant and drinking it can refresh the lungs. The Yan River (also known as Zhai River) meanders along the side, resembling a divine dragon winding through the green mountains. When I walked to Yan, I washed my hands and feet in it several times. Although the water is deep, it still makes people want to linger. Other scenic spots include Huadong West Cliff 3 li west of the city, Zhongping South Barrier 1 li south of the city, Douji Xiaoyue 40 li west of the city, Phoenix Ridge Qinglan east of the city gate, Jiuquan Tianniang behind the Confucian temple, Oil Well Boyong outside the west gate city railing, Suyuyu Waterfall 1 li east of the city, and Jiu Lian Chuanzhu 15 li west of the city. Eight beautiful landscapes surround Yanchang. Although Yan is small, it is enough to be proud of. Residents outside the city mostly live in kilns. Those living in the plains mostly live in stone kilns, and those living on the mountain tops mostly live in earth kilns. About one-third of the clothes are made of local cloth, and one-third are made of cloth from Shanxi. Most of the drinking water is spring water, and residents on the mountain tops mostly store water in kilns for emergencies. The Yan River still has no strange taste, and residents mostly use it for washing. About 50 li west of the city is Black Drum Heap (an earth mountain) with a grove of cypress trees, covering about 10 mu. About 2 li west of the city along the Yan River is Silin Ping, which can irrigate about 300 to 400 mu, greatly benefiting the farmers.

The entire county has three senior elementary schools (including one girls' school), with a total of 120 students, of which only 10 are girls. There are 22 junior elementary schools, with a total of about 300 students, of which 30 to 40 are girls. There is one people's school with about 10 students. Teachers' monthly salaries are about 10 yuan or more. The annual education expenses for junior elementary schools are about 3,000 yuan, which are raised by the Education Bureau. Senior elementary schools have a fund of 4,000 yuan, with an annual interest of 800 to 900 yuan. In addition to temporary solutions, the annual cost of people's education is about 1,400 yuan, and the annual education administrative expenses are about 800 yuan. In addition, 450 yuan of the annual interest of 1,500 yuan is used as an annual subsidy for further education. Those sent to Peking for study are about three people, those studying in Shanxi are three people (female students),

one is at the Central Military Academy. In addition, some people are sent to Yulin, Xi'an, and other places to study higher knowledge.

Coal from the kiln costs about 3 jiao per 100 catties, and the market price is about 7 jiao per 100 catties. Oil

costs about 2 jiao 5 fen per catty. The atmosphere seems more open-minded than in other places. A considerable number of young girls have cut their hair and do not bind their feet.

One evening, all circles in Yanchang held a welcome meeting at the County First Senior Elementary School. I did not attend due to a cold. Many members of the delegation have been suffering from minor ailments recently, so we planned to rest for another day on the 2nd. On the morning of the 3rd, we started to turn south and head towards Yichuan. (Sent from Yanchang on September 2nd)

▲ Mood Swings Again

On our second day in Yanchang, September 2nd, although the morning sun still sang brightly to the distant guests, the crimson sunlight still shone all over the earth, and the donkeys and horses tied to the wasteland still moaned mournfully, the mountains were still green, and the water still flowed, this day of leisure aroused our infinite homesickness. Although all of our environment was the same, most of us naturally felt a burning desire to return home. Everything in front of us seemed to have changed rapidly. Although some of us had wireless radios, we could not receive any news due to the high mountains separating us. So, troubles came, depression arose, and the peaceful minds that had been like ancient wells were now having mood swings again.

Because the exploration of Yanchang's oil had been completed on the first day, we felt that we had nothing to do on the second day. In the morning, flies were flying around the room, which was very rampant. They disturbed us so that we could not eat or sleep peacefully. So, we found three or four fly swatters and launched a war against them. As a result, of course, the people were victorious. About a thousand flies died, their corpses littered the ground, and their ability to harass was temporarily suppressed. In the afternoon, we went to the Yan River outside the city to bathe in the torrent. The water was clear and cool, and we felt very happy after bathing. In the evening, everyone wanted to hold a pastime meeting, but it was unsuccessful. In about eighteen days after we set off, this day was the most boring and the most incredible.

Local Correspondence Songjiang

▲ Telegrams Contend for Honest Collection of Land Survey Fees This county previously received a provincial order to levy land survey funds at 1 jiao per mu, with less than 1 mu calculated as 1 mu. It was requested at the administrative meeting that it be reduced to 5 fen to meet the 1% limit, but it was not approved. An order was issued to issue separate receipts for collection. However, the local people believe that charging for less than 1 mu as 1 mu increases the burden and have requested the provincial department to collect honestly in accordance with the land price tax collection regulations. The following is a telegram from citizen Wu Weihe and others to the provincial government, the Ministry of Finance, and the Ministry of Construction: (Having been ordered to collect land survey fees at 1 jiao per mu, with less than 1 mu counted as 1 mu, and earnestly instructed that if there is extra collection, they will be allowed to sue at any time, etc., which is inexplicably frightening. Checking the land price tax collection of mu donations, all are collected honestly according to the number of mu completed, and there has never been an example of rounding up and adding a burden to the people. Moreover, the amount of the printed strings is mostly odd numbers. If they are all rounded up, it will inevitably be like draining the pond to catch the fish and lose the principle of equal tax burden. As for the entire county of Song, the amount of tax strings reaches more than 200,000 per period. How many are odd numbers and how many are integers? It is difficult to collect if you do not collect statistics, and it is easy to open up the gradual trend of bribery among tax collectors. And knowing Qingyi's method, 9 jiao and 1 fen of land survey fees are collected for every two taels of silver, which are also collected honestly according to the number of mu, which is very clear. Rounding up in Songyi seems to lose equality and violates the purpose of not allowing extra collection. We respectfully ask your seat to think about the people's suffering and still follow the established case of collection and collect honestly according to the number of mu completed for each string, so as to prevent all malpractices, etc.) Now there are many who continue to request. I think the provincial department will be able to comply with the people's wishes.

Suzhou

▲A Woman Gives Birth to Triplets. Mrs. Zhu Lu, residing at No. 18 Xihui outside Qimen, is 27 years old this year. Her husband works as a clerk in a pawnshop. Recently, she became pregnant and had not given birth for a long time, and her abdomen was unusually large. She went to the Tianci Zhuang Boxi Hospital to await delivery. At 10 a.m. yesterday (the 22nd), she suddenly gave birth to triplets. Both mother and children are currently safe.

▲Lü Ziwen's Three Suicide Notes. Lü Ziwen, the 21-year-old daughter of Shanghai merchant Lü Shenfu, married Yuan Junli, a wealthy man at No. 38 Daxin Bridge outside Panmen, Suzhou, last September. Because Yuan's family affairs were managed by the late husband's widowed daughter-in-law, Tong Baozhen, Ms. Lü was forced to commit suicide. Yesterday (the 23rd), the deceased's family discovered wounds on her arm and requested the court to conduct a re-examination, hoping to punish the ungrateful husband and stepmother according to the law to redress this strange injustice. Ms. Lü left many suicide notes and diaries, excerpts of which are as follows: (1) To her parents: "Yesterday (the 19th), Junli forced me to write a note, and Baozhen forced me to say certain things. In the evening, they wanted me to write another note, but I refused, so they beat my hands and legs. My heart is so pained. Junli said he wouldn't stop until I wrote it, otherwise he would beat me every day until I couldn't live in peace. As for the previous time I wanted to have a medical examination, Junli said if you go for an examination, I will first publish a divorce notice. Alas, my parents, your daughter really cannot continue to be wrong. Farewell, please take care." (2) To her husband, Yuan Junli: "You said I have lost my virginity, but I have not. I said I would go with you for an examination, but you refused. You forced me to write a note, or you would divorce me. Because I cannot explain clearly, I can only die, awaiting official examination." (3) To all circles: "My husband said I am unchaste, hence my suicide. Please kind-hearted gentlemen, retrieve my body and ask the officials for an examination," etc. As for her diary, it describes the family situation, mostly about how her husband Junli and stepmother conspired to abuse her, and Junli's indifference towards her.

Wuxi

▲The Construction Bureau Hastens the Construction of the Shanghai-Wuxi Highway. Among the roads in Jiangsu Province and its counties that have been built, in addition to the Beijing-Hangzhou National Highway, there are the Beijing-Zhenjiang-Wuxi-Changzhou Provincial Highway, and the Wuxi-Chengjiang, Wuxi-Yi, Wuxi-Yi county roads. The local county's highway, starting from the starting point of the Wuxi-Changzhou Provincial Highway, can now directly reach the capital and connect with the Beijing-Hangzhou National Highway. However, the Shanghai-Wuxi Provincial Highway from Wuxi to Shanghai has not yet been realized due to limited funding. Recently, the Military Affairs Commission believes that the construction of the Shanghai-Wuxi Highway is urgently needed, so it has specifically instructed the Jiangsu Provincial Construction Bureau to start construction immediately and complete it within the shortest possible time, so that the Wuxi-Changzhou Provincial Highway can directly reach the capital. Director Dong Xiu-jia, after receiving the order, has now made proper plans and specially dispatched Zhang Jingming, a technical officer of the bureau, to lead surveyors to begin surveying. Mr. Zhang, upon receiving the order, departed for Wuxi to investigate the starting point of the highway. It is stipulated that the section from Wuxi to Suzhou will follow the original road along the embankment and widen it, while the section from Suzhou to Shanghai will need to open up a new road along the Beijing-Shanghai Railway. It is said that the survey period will take about one month before it can be completed, and then bidding for construction will be invited.

▲Capture of Robbers in the Central Bank Robbery Case. The Investigation Department of the Capital Garrison Headquarters, having learned that the Central Bank robbers had fled to Dagang Town, secretly dispatched several officers and two squads of soldiers to Dagang Town, where they captured the four main criminals in their den. Nantong

▲Water Police Ordered to Monitor Fishing Protection Team. The Fisheries Administration Bureau of the Ministry of Industry previously established an office in Nantong, ordering fishermen to register and collect license fees, and also dispatched a fishing protection team and the Qing'an warship to be stationed in Yaogang. Currently, the Fourth District Department of the Water Police, upon the order of the Civil Affairs Department, believes that Nantong City is not a fishing area, and there is no need to set up an office. Furthermore, it is rumored that the Qing'an warship has engaged in improper behavior on the harbor surface. District Chief Zhang is ordered to send a team to monitor the actions of the fishing protection team. The department also dispatched the Junhe warship to Nantong to assist in handling the matter. The Junhe warship arrived in Yaogang on the 22nd. District Chief Zhang of the Water Police immediately sent personnel to the Fisheries Administration Bureau office at noon on the 22nd, requesting them to comply with the department's order to withdraw. At the same time, a team was sent to Yaogang to jointly monitor the actions of the Qing'an warship with the Junhe warship and ordered it to return to Nanjing immediately.

▲Fourth Prison to Expand Housing. Sun, the warden of the Nantong Fourth Prison, believes that due to the increasing number of prisoners, expansion is necessary. He previously formulated a plan requiring 20,000 yuan and submitted it to the Higher Court for review. Warden Sun also personally went to the Zhenjiang Finance Department and the Suzhou Higher Court a few days ago to discuss the matter. The results were quite satisfactory. The Higher Court agreed to allocate half of the expansion funds, and the remaining 10,000 yuan will be raised locally through donations. As for the prisoner rations after the expansion, Director Shu of the Finance Department also agreed to increase the number from 300 to 400. Warden Sun returned to Nantong on the 22nd and is currently planning to raise donations and invite bids for construction.

Jiaxing

▲Middle and Primary School Principals Petition the County Government. Due to tax revenue shortages, the education funds in Jiaxing are insufficient to cover expenditures. Qiu Shouchi, the Director of the Finance Bureau, is also unable to assume the responsibility of raising funds. Therefore, salaries have been in arrears for many months. On the 22nd, the principals, together with the district education officers, petitioned the County Magistrate and the Director of the Finance Bureau. County Magistrate Jiang promised to discuss the matter further at the county government meeting. All the principals stated that if there is no solution, they will jointly submit their resignations.

Xiaoshan

▲Murder of Husband Case Returned to Original County for Execution. In June, Cao Cai of Shicun outside the South Gate of Xiaoshan, a merchant, was murdered by his wife, Cao Cai, who colluded with her lover, Xu Arong, to cut off Cao Caisheng's genitals. After the criminal was apprehended, the Xiaoshan County Court sentenced her to death. Cao Cai was not satisfied and appealed. Now, the third trial has concluded, and the death sentence has been upheld. After the Higher Court presented the case to the provincial government for approval, the criminal was returned to her place of origin to be executed by hanging and shooting soon.

▲Tragic News of Two Children Burned to Death in a Fire in Xixiang. The home of Sun Youxing, a resident of Zhengjiahu in Xixiang, Xiaoshan, caught fire at night on the 20th due to carelessness with fire in the kitchen. The fire quickly spread to three two-story buildings, five thatched houses, and two single-story buildings, and tragically burned to death a three-year-old boy and a five-year-old girl. Other losses of miscellaneous items, rice, etc., are estimated to be worth over 5,000 yuan.

▲High Tide Causes Multiple Drownings. The Qiantang River's autumn tide has been especially strong recently. On the afternoon of the 20th, two fishing boats near Yandong Jiangzui were approaching the tide when they accidentally capsized. All nine boatmen, both adults and children, fell into the water. Despite strenuous rescue efforts, three people are still missing and presumed drowned. On the same day, a general merchandise boat near Xixing shore was also hit by the tide and sank. All the cloth and paper goods, worth about 8,000 to 9,000 yuan, sank to the bottom of the river. Four boatmen fell into the water, and one drowned.

In addition to enclosing the certificate and a list of representatives, please bring the certificate with you when attending."

Teachers from Chinese Schools in British Malaya Expelled and Arrive in Shanghai

In recent years, the British Malaya has severely suppressed overseas Chinese education. Various social, historical, and geographical textbooks related to criticizing foreigners in primary and secondary schools have been banned. Teachers often fear walking on thin ice. Recently, Dong Lianduo and Shen Shifang, teachers at the Pengting Guandan Overseas Chinese School, were expelled again. They arrived in Shanghai yesterday from Hong Kong by ship. According to them, on April 24, the Director of Studies went to the school to search and found only one paper in a student's drawer: a notice of the previous year's flood in China, in which families and students were urged to save on sweets and donate to the disaster relief fund. There was also a paper advising families to boycott Japanese goods after the September 18th Incident, an entry in a student's diary commemorating the seventy-two martyrs of Huanghuagang, and several news items about the Northeast Army's Ma Zhanshan's battles. Three songs, including the memorial song for the Premier, the Chinese Kuomintang party song, and the May 9th National Humiliation Day song, were found in a song copybook. The local government considered these to have political implications and ordered their arrest and imprisonment on May 21, forbidding bail and visits from outsiders. Photos and fingerprints were taken, and the situation was very serious. They were detained for more than ten days, handcuffed, and escorted to the prison in Lipi, the capital of Pengheng Province. They were tried in prison by the San Si Council of the Overseas Chinese Education Administration, without allowing witnesses to be heard or anyone to observe, which was even stricter than the treatment of murderers and robbers. After the trial, the charges and reasons were not announced. Later, through the rescue of the school board and the intercession of the consul stationed in Singapore with the chief of the San Si Council, they were allowed to be deported on bail. On August 18, they left on the Dejiada mail ship, with tickets directly to Shanghai. On the 23rd, when the ship arrived in Hong Kong, the police came on board and arrested them, claiming that they had committed a crime in Hong Kong. They were re-imprisoned. On the 23rd, the Hong Kong government deported them again. The case was handled by two governments, and they spent four months in prison. It was indeed tragic. All our compatriots cannot help but shed tears of sympathy for them. If we do not rise up and resist, overseas Chinese education will be in danger! (Xinsheng News Agency)

Austrian Olympic Committee Member Departs Shanghai This Morning

▲Committee Visited War Relics Yesterday Morning | Gave Public Speech in the Afternoon

▲Mayor Wu Hosted a Banquet in the Evening | Departs for Europe This Morning

Mr. Schmidt, an Austrian member of the World Olympic Congress, Mr. Massoli, a Swiss member, and Dr. Li Mi, a Swiss physical education professor, arrived in China for a tour. Yesterday was their second day in Shanghai. In the morning, the city government sent escorts to accompany them to visit the war relics in Zhabei and Wusong. In the afternoon, they attended a public lecture organized by the city government at the YMCA. In the evening, Mayor Wu hosted a banquet at the Xing Hua Lou restaurant and watched a performance at the Tianchan Theater. The three committee members will take the French postal ship "Athos" this morning to return to Europe by sea. The following is a record of their travels yesterday:

▲Visiting the War Relics of Shanghai-Songhu

At around 9:00 a.m., the city government sent Chen Yuze, Tian Heqing, and others to accompany the three committee members to visit Zhabei and Wusong. Austrian member Schmidt was unable to attend due to other matters, so only the two Swiss members went. They expressed unlimited sympathy to our country regarding the Japanese army's atrocities.

▲Public Lecture at the YMCA

At 1:00 p.m., the city government hosted a public lecture at the auditorium of the YMCA at Eight Immortals Bridge. The audience was full, with over six hundred young men and women. Shen Siliang first introduced the two Austrian and Swiss members, who then delivered brief speeches as follows:

▲Schmidt Speaks on Austrian Sports - President of the Austrian National Amateur Sports Association, member of the World Olympic Committee, and Austrian business representative to the Geneva League of Nations, Schmidt, began by saying that his speech would be divided into three parts: (1) the state of Austrian sports, (2) Austria and the Olympics, and (3) China and the Olympics. He said that after the European War, Austria was divided, and the vast territory is now only the area between the Alps and the Danube River, with a population of six million, two million of whom live in Vienna. This small population can be considered quite large in Europe. There are a total of 23 sports associations nationwide, with 94,000 members. In Vienna, there is the Austrian National Sports Association. In general, due to geographical factors, the main types of sports can be divided into four: (1) ice skating, (2) weightlifting, (3) boxing, and (4) fencing. Other sports are also practiced. This time, they participated in the Olympics in the United States despite the country's extreme economic difficulties. The government did not donate a single penny, and all funds came from private donations, so they only sent nine athletes and three staff members. Fortunately, they did not disgrace their mission and won a women's fencing championship, a second place in weightlifting, and three third places. As for the important significance of the Olympics, it can be divided into three points: first, absolute equality on the sports field; second, separation from all political relations; and third, the noble amateur principle, not for money, but for the honor of the group they represent. Therefore, this year, in 1932, they were able to see the flag of the Blue Sky and White Sun in Los Angeles, and they were all welcomed with applause. Everything is difficult at the beginning, and we deeply know the current internal and external difficulties of China, but the small number of representatives of China have done their best in Los Angeles. What is especially worth mentioning is the effort of Mr. Shen Siliang of the delegation. It is hoped that a larger delegation from China will be seen at the next Berlin Olympics. The Austrian sports community is very willing to cooperate with China and is preparing at all times to meet China's needs. Austria is a relatively advanced country in sports. If China needs talents to guide new methods in weightlifting, boxing, and fencing, Austria is very willing to contribute, and so on.

▲Massoli Talks About Swiss Sports - Next, Swiss Olympic Committee member Massoli spoke in French about Swiss sports, saying that Switzerland is the oldest democracy in the world, but also the smallest. The country has a population of four million, with about 25,000 sports association members. In the 13th century, due to the oppression of foreign enemies, the youth of the whole country actively promoted sports to strengthen their physique. After 200 years of training, the foundation is still deep. In terms of national relations, Switzerland and Austria had many conflicts in the past, but on the sports field, they still work hand in hand. This time, due to economic and distance reasons, very few athletes were sent to the Olympics, and nothing was gained. However, in 1928, three silver shields were won. Committee member Ma also mentioned Switzerland's contribution to culture and the motivation of the Olympics, the past sessions, and seeing China participate in this tenth session. He hoped that China could send more athletes to the next session in Berlin, and so on.

▲City First Stadium Performs National Arts - The Swiss Consul in Shanghai, Wu Kemoluo, also stood up to extend his warm hospitality. Finally, the City First Stadium performed various national arts, which were greatly appreciated by the committee members.

▲Mayor Wu Hosted a Banquet Last Night

Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng hosted a banquet at the Xing Hua Lou Restaurant at 8:00 p.m. last night to welcome the Austrian and Swiss committee members. The consuls of Austria and Switzerland in Shanghai, as well as Zhao Jinqing, Shen Siliang, Ling Xichu, and others from the sports community, attended, accompanied by Secretary Yu Hongjun of the city government and the heads of various bureaus. The banquet ended at almost 11:00 p.m., and then Mayor Wu accompanied them to the Tianchan Theater to watch a play, as the committee members greatly appreciated Chinese martial arts, saying that they have a very important place in sports. The following is a record of the speeches given during the banquet:

▲Mayor Wu's Speech - I welcome you all in my capacity as the Mayor of Shanghai, and I am deeply honored. Today, the politicians and diplomats of the world are thinking about and seeking to solve the question of why the world is fighting and restless. The nations of the world are fighting every day, and thus a narrow nationalism is gradually formed. The struggles of the world are becoming more intense, and the unrest in the world is becoming more serious. However, stabilizing the world is a mutual responsibility of mankind. Although what we seek may not be an ideal utopia, the World Games is one of the effective ways to connect the world, unite the world, and stabilize the world. This time in the United States, our country sent very few representatives. I sincerely hope to send a larger delegation to the next session, so as to do our best to connect the world, unite the world, and seek world peace. And what I hope more from the two committee members is to tell the people of your countries about the good impressions in China. China is a nation that loves peace. The ancient sages taught that all within the four seas are brothers. I would like to use this wine to wish you all a safe journey.

▲Schmidt's Reply - Austrian Committee member Schmidt stood up and gave a reply, saying that he was very grateful for the Mayor's hospitality. It is even more gratifying that the Mayor can pay attention to the relationship between the Olympic Games and world peace. However, to achieve this goal, we still need to work hard. This time, we deeply know the difficulties that China is currently experiencing. The number of representatives does not matter. I hope that more representatives can be sent to participate in the next session. As for the development of sports, it is also deeply related to the social aspect. What we sincerely hope from the Mayor is to be a good friend of our sports community.

The Swiss committee member also gave a brief speech, and the Swiss Consul stood up again to express his thanks. The banquet ended in a joyful atmosphere.

As for your request, once a suitable method is considered, with the best of our ability, we will immediately raise funds and donate them to the Northeast Volunteer Army to meet urgent needs.
