Unified Tax September 55.4

The Truth Behind the Tragic Death of Driver Jiang Haitao of the Special Court

▲ Another Driver Dismissed by the Court

▲ Suspected that Jiang Provoked Resentment

▲ Paid 200 Yuan to Hire a Murderer

▲ Trial Concluded Yesterday, Debate Ended

Jiang Haitao, who worked as a driver in the First Special District Court and resided at No. 130 Shanjia Garden, Guling Road, left home at 8:30 a.m. on the 15th of this month to go to work at the court. However, after walking only a few steps, Zhang Zimei from Tongzhou suddenly followed behind him and made suspicious movements. Jiang noticed this and ran forward. Zhang pursued relentlessly. Jiang tripped and fell. Zhang caught up, pulled out a sharp bayonet, and stabbed Jiang seven times, causing critical injuries. Blood gushed out, and Jiang collapsed to the ground, dying shortly after. Seeing his goal achieved, Zhang turned and fled. Pedestrian Dai Shengrong and watchman No. 277 happened to witness the incident and helped to apprehend Zhang. A knife sheath was found near him, but the murder weapon was discarded halfway by Zhang and recovered by someone, who handed it to the police. The knife was stained with blood. Subsequently, Chinese Detective Zhu Mengwei and Western Detective Pei Naiduo arrived and took Zhang and the knife to the Xinzha Police Station. The deceased's body was taken to the morgue for examination. After confirming the body, the widow, Jiang Zhu, was instructed to arrange for the coffin and burial. The arrest and investigation of the murderer have already been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Zhang Zimei was escorted by the police station to the Second Criminal Court of the Special Court. The police station's lawyer, Wang Yaotang, rose to present the case, stating that Zhang was being prosecuted under Article 284, Section 1 of the Criminal Law for premeditated murder. The case occurred at 8:30 a.m. on the 15th of this month. Witness Dai Shengrong was walking on Guling Road when he suddenly heard the sound of two people chasing each other behind him. Soon, they passed Dai. The person behind (the defendant) shouted, "Catch the thief!" and the person in front (the deceased) suddenly fell. The defendant caught up, pulled out a bayonet, and stabbed him seven times before fleeing. Dai was shocked and immediately chased after him. At the intersection of Xizang Road and Guling Road, he saw the defendant discard the murder weapon on the ground, which was picked up by a pedestrian and handed to the police. At that time, watchman No. 277 also helped chase the defendant and apprehended him at the intersection of Beijing Road and Xizang Road. However, the defendant still resisted, causing a knife sheath to fall from his waistband, which matched the bayonet handed over by the police. He was then taken to the police station. The defendant's clothes were also stained with blood, which was presented as evidence along with the murder weapon. Furthermore, the police station's investigation revealed that the defendant was instigated by Lu Baosheng to murder Jiang Haitao. Lu and Jiang were colleagues, both working as drivers in the First Special Court. Lu was suddenly dismissed by the court, and he suspected that Jiang had provoked this, causing him to harbor resentment. He instructed the defendant to murder Jiang, promising a reward of 200 yuan. Lu also provided the bayonet to the defendant. After the incident, the police went to Lu's home in Garden Square, Jin Shenfu Road, but could not find him. It was later learned that Lu, after being dismissed by the court, was working as a driver in the Second Special Court. They went to the Second Special Court to investigate. It was reported that Lu was indeed a driver, but he had taken sick leave two weeks prior and had not returned, making it impossible to arrest him. The widow, Jiang Zhu, also complained that her husband had died tragically and requested justice. Witnesses Dai Shengrong, Jin Kuitang, and Xie Huilian testified that they witnessed the situation at the time. Watchman No. 277 also testified that when apprehending the defendant, he punched the defendant in the back, and the knife sheath fell from his belt at that time. When questioned, the defendant denied killing Jiang Haitao, claiming that he was passing by the area that day and collided with Dai, resulting in four or five people beating him and handing him over to the police. The court appointed lawyer Wu Linkun to provide free legal defense for the defendant, arguing that according to the testimonies and records, the defendant did not have premeditated murder, and he should be sentenced for manslaughter. The police station's lawyer, Wang Yaotang, argued that the defendant had confessed in the police station, which was consistent with the facts, and the evidence was sufficient, requesting a death sentence according to the law. Judge Ge Shixun reviewed the case and announced the end of the debate, scheduling the sentencing for the following Friday. The defendant was remanded in custody.

Two Boys Run Over and Killed by Cars

▲ Yesterday at 3:50 PM, a Chinese area Concession No. 3743/International Settlement Concession No. 17146 automobile, traveling on Hengfeng Road and approaching the Qingzhao Road intersection, suddenly encountered a child running across the road. The driver, Wu Qiusheng, was unable to avoid the child due to excessive speed, resulting in the child being knocked down. The wheels ran over the child's head, and the child, wearing , died instantly. Police officer Wang Hanlin, who was on duty nearby, witnessed the incident and immediately stopped the vehicle and detained the driver, taking them to the Second Precinct of the Fourth District. After interrogation, a written report was submitted, and the deceased's family member, Dai Zhang, was summoned. She stated that the deceased was her son, named Shuangxi, sixteen years old.

▲ Yesterday around 3:00 PM, in front of the Shanghai Electric Tramways Company on Yangshupu Road, a child, approximately ten years old, wearing a dark blue serge short shirt, white cloth pants, and satin shoes, resembling a child from a wealthy family, was wandering in the road. A cargo truck sped by and struck the child, running over his head, resulting in instant death. Western police officer No. 286 arrived on patrol, recorded the vehicle number, and sent the deceased child to the Tongren Hospital, before transferring him to the morgue to await examination by the court.

Police Informant Killed

▲ A Thief Apprehended in Xiaobangnei

The day before yesterday at approximately 3:00 PM, Wang Tianxiong, a patrol officer from the Second Precinct of the Fourth District of Zhabei, received a report from informant Dai Fushou that a notorious bandit was hiding in a straw shed behind the Chongxin Yarn Factory in Xiaobangnei, Laobasheng Road. Patrol Officer Wang immediately led the informant and Jiang Haifeng and others to the location. As soon as they approached the straw shed, they were spotted by the bandit, who immediately opened fire to resist arrest. The loud shot struck informant Dai Fushou in a vital area, causing him to fall to the ground and die instantly. Patrol Officer Wang and others immediately pursued the bandit to Xiaobangnei, where they apprehended a notorious bandit named Jin Dasanzi. As the location was in the Sixth District, they reported the incident to the Sixth District and then took the bandit back to the station. They immediately ordered the local land guard to report to the local court for an inquest. Yesterday, the court dispatched Prosecutor Yang with the coroner and others to the scene. The examination revealed that the deceased had two gunshot wounds in the chest, confirming that he had been shot to death. The family was instructed to claim the body for coffin and burial.

Woman Commits Suicide Due to Anger and Frustration

Cui Qianji, from Hubei, 38 years old, operated a cigarette paper and money exchange stall at No. 107 Avenue Edward VII in the French Concession, at the Guangtailai Inn. His wife, Wei, also 38 and from the same hometown, lived with him and their three children (one daughter and two sons) in Room 87 on the third floor of Guangtailai. Wei, feeling emotionally distressed, secretly ingested raw opium the day before yesterday. The poison took effect at 8:00 PM that night, and her husband discovered her. She was sent to Renji Hospital, but due to the severity of the poisoning, treatment was ineffective. She died at 2:30 AM yesterday. The hospital notified the police, who sent the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Mortuary for an autopsy. According to her husband, Cui Qianji, his wife's suicide was caused by Zhang Yuehua (from Guangdong), the wife of Wang Ziyuan (from Yunnan), who lived in Room 90. Wang held a position in the government and had gone to Yantai to seek employment, leaving his wife, Zhang, alone in Shanghai. Wei became familiar with Zhang due to their proximity. Seeing that Zhang was cooking her own meals, which was inconvenient, Wei kindly invited her to share meals with their family. However, a malicious person spread rumors, telling Zhang that Wei was saying that Zhang was stingy and not paying for her meals. Zhang, misled by these false words, did not investigate the truth and repeatedly insulted and scolded Wei. Wei, an honest person, felt unjustly accused and unable to vent her anger, leading her to suicidal thoughts. On the 17th, she went to the Bund on Fourth Avenue to throw herself into the Huangpu River, but a police officer spotted her, stopped her, and took her to the police station, who sent her home. After repeated persuasion, she remained unable to overcome her grief and did not abandon her suicidal intentions. The day before yesterday, she ingested poison and committed suicide. Yesterday, the police reported the incident to the Second Special Court, who dispatched Prosecutor Deng Baosun to the mortuary. After examining the body and hearing the husband's account of the deceased's unjust suicide, Deng ruled that Cui Wei had indeed died from ingesting poison. The body was claimed by her husband, Cui Qianji, for burial. It is reported that Zhang Yuehua, realizing her mistake, has asked someone to mediate a settlement with the deceased's family.

Dong Kang Investigates Impersonation for Soliciting Donations

A letter from Dong Kang to the Garrison Headquarters to investigate impersonation for soliciting donations: Respectfully to the Garrison Headquarters, I was recently shown a letter by Secretary Xu of your headquarters, inquiring about someone soliciting factory donations in my name. I was extremely surprised to hear this. Since my lawyer, Xie Zheng, settled in Shanghai, he has been engaged in editing and teaching and does not participate in any political or public welfare activities. There are many strange cases of fraud and deception in Shanghai. I urge your headquarters to conduct a thorough investigation and send the culprit to court for legal action. Furthermore, my residence's telephone number is 32371. If similar incidents occur again, please instruct the driver to inquire about the accurate number, and the truth will come to light. Respectfully, Lawyer Dong Kang of the Songhu Garrison Headquarters, September 22nd.

Red Pill Den Cracked on Jiangxi Road

Chief Detective Lu Dagong of the General Police Station learned that someone was privately operating an opium den for people to smoke red pills at No. 250 Mingchang Lane, Jiangxi Road. He reported this to the First Special Court, which issued a search warrant. The day before yesterday, he, along with Western Detective Glover, secretly went to the location with Chinese and Western police officers and apprehended Chen Qingzeng (from Shanghai), who was operating the opium den, and a woman named Gu Zhou. Two respectable businessmen were caught in the act of smoking opium. One was Chen Yuanjin, from Ningbo, residing at No. 63 Huade Road, currently working as a clerk at the Welfare Company, and the other was Ni Zhiyao, also from Ningbo, residing at No. 57 Yipin Lane, Xindagu Road, currently working as a clerk at the British Tahe Foreign Firm, and the beloved son-in-law of Sun Yunqing, the famous Qinglian Pavilion Master in Shanghai. Another man named Ding Jinfa, also from Ningbo, was of unknown occupation. Two opium pipes, two opium lamps, and a large quantity of red pills were confiscated. The five opium offenders (male and female) were taken to the police station and detained separately. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the First Criminal Court of the First Special Court. Police Station Lawyer Qian Xunji presented the case, accusing Gu Zhou and Chen Qingzeng of violating Article 10 of the Prohibition of Opium Law, and Chen Yuanjin, Ni Zhiyao, and Ding Jinfa of violating Article 11 of the same law, requesting that they be punished according to the law. Presiding Judge Feng briefly questioned the defendants and sentenced Chen Qingzeng and Gu Zhou to eight months imprisonment each, with a fine of 80 yuan. Chen Yuanjin, Ni Zhiyao, and Ding Jinfa were each sentenced to one month imprisonment, with a fine of 40 yuan. The opium paraphernalia was confiscated. Sun Yunqing was also present in court during the interrogation.

Ma Run Ji Fur Shop at No. 523 Guangdong Road was broken into by multiple robbers late at night on November 11, 1929 (Republic of China Year 18). Armed with handguns, they stole furs worth over 2,300 yuan and fled. The shop reported the incident with reports No. 1313 and No. 1473 to the Chinese police. Chinese police officers No. 1313 and No. 1473 were guarding outside, so when the thieves exited, they encountered the police. The thieves immediately opened fire, injuring a Chinese officer from No. 173 in the hand. The thieves scattered and escaped without being apprehended. Liu Junqing and Chen Yonggui, Chinese detectives from the Laozha Police Station, learned that a Shandong man named Chen Yuanzhen (also known as Chen Ganting) was the leader of the robbery and was hiding at No. 351 Qinghe Lane, Guangdong Road. They secretly went there at 5:00 PM the day before yesterday and apprehended Chen. They confiscated a fur coat lining and 352 yuan in cash, which were taken to the police station and detained. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the First Criminal Court of the First Special Court. Police Station Lawyer Qian Xunji prosecuted Chen according to Article 348 of the Criminal Code, stating that the police station had not yet fully investigated the case and requested an extension of one week. The plaintiff, Ma Shaoqing, testified that the defendant was the leader who directed the robbery. Shanghai War Zone Relief Association Passes Relief Fund Distribution Measures

The 11th meeting of the Shanghai War Zone Relief Association was attended by Wang Binyan, Pan Gongzhan, Shen Tianxin, Ma Shaoquan, Huang Boqiao, Zheng Tonghe, Hong Lanxiang, Wen Hongen, Cai Zengji, Yu Hongjun, Li Denghui, Wang Yiting, Yin Rugeng, Hu Hongji, Yu Qiaqing, and others, chaired by Wu Tiecheng. The following matters were discussed: (1) Relief fund distribution measures: Resolved and passed, but 20,000 yuan must be allocated from the poverty relief loan and housing construction loan items as relief funds for secondary schools in the city affected by the disaster. (2) Draft regulations for the War Zone Temporary Relief Loan Office: Resolved and passed with revisions. (3) Budget for the equipment expenses of the War Zone Temporary Relief Loan Office: Resolved and passed. (4) Budget for the recurring expenses of the War Zone Temporary Relief Loan Office: Resolved and sent to the municipal government for review and approval. (5) Relief for secondary schools in the city affected by the disaster: Resolved that 20,000 yuan be allocated from the poverty relief loan and housing construction loan items, and another 20,000 yuan be raised by the association as the first batch of relief funds. (6) Funding for the restoration of the Wusong Seaside Public Hospital: Resolved to task the relief group with working with the Health Bureau and the Wusong Municipal Committee to formulate a plan and submit it to the association for review and approval.

News from the Chinese Medical Association Conference

The Chinese Medical Association will hold its annual conference from the 28th of this month to the 5th of next month at the Lester Institute on Avenue Road, Shanghai. The association is the only national medical research organization. Since taking over the Bo Medical Association this May, the first step in unifying medical organizations has been successfully completed. Chinese and Western members each constitute half of the membership, breaking down international boundaries in the academic field. This conference, being the first after the merger, is of great significance, including the election of officers and the approval of regulations. The conference agenda has already been printed and distributed to members. The Lester Institute, being the only medical research institute in China, is magnificent and well-equipped. The newly constructed building has just been completed and is being used as the conference venue, which is convenient. It is reported that the first day of the conference agenda will be for registration of attending members. In the evening, a welcome reception will be held at the YMCA on Min Ti Ni Yin Road, inviting party and government officials to deliver speeches. Starting from the second day, business meetings will be held every morning, and departmental group meetings will be held in the afternoons. The content of the papers will be very thorough. Lunch will be provided by the association and will be held in the shed behind the venue. After lunch, various medical and health films will be shown to enhance the atmosphere. The group meetings will begin at 2:00 PM. It is reported that the Public Health Department of the Public Concession and the National Seaport Quarantine Bureau have invited members attending the conference to visit their respective workplaces to learn from each other. The remaining rooms of the conference venue will be used for product displays on the first floor, featuring various pharmaceutical and the latest equipment and supplies. The second floor will be used for health education displays, featuring exhibits from the Ministry of Health of the Interior and the Public Health Department of the Public Concession, which are quite eye-catching. It is also reported that the association welcomes people from the medical and pharmaceutical fields to visit, and welcomes all members and non-members.

Oil Market

White Tung Oil Prices Have Stabilized

The market for white tung oil has long been weak and short-lived since the gradual decline in foreign sales from Hankou. There have been no significant improvements this year. Prices have hovered around 17-18 taels for foreign sales and 14-15 taels domestically. Compared to the price fluctuations of 7-8 taels or even 10 taels four or five years ago, the difference is like the sky and the earth. The rapid change in the market is truly immeasurable. It was recently reported that foreign firms sold some at 17 taels and 7 qian, but only in quantities of dozens or hundreds of tons. It is rumored that foreign firms still have some small appetite, but Chinese firms want to increase the price slightly, which foreign firms are unwilling to do. The increase would only be a few qian. This shows how small the price fluctuations are. Domestic sales fell to 14 taels and 4.6 qian, and sales were also low, making it difficult to determine prosperity or decline. However, prices are already low, and customers hope for improvement, so even if the price increases, it will be slight. Therefore, based on the current market, it is still difficult to turn things around. However, new goods will enter the market in the coming year when provinces report their quantities, which should bring changes. There is still more than a month before the new products are released. Because domestic sales have fallen, local firms in Shanghai are not paying attention to imports. Transactions in the market are even quieter than before. It is reported that 4,000 dan of Xiangtong oil have recently arrived in Hankou, with an opening price of 14 taels and 2 qian. The oil from this route is older and is intended for other destinations, not the Shanghai market, so there has been no procurement. However, the festival season has passed, and even if some supplies are desired, they must be selected from Hankou and Hangzhou.

Piece Goods

Domestic Woolens Selling Well

Domestic woolens have been increasing in production recently, and sales have also been expanding. Woolens are currently selling particularly well. The wide and narrow striped camel woolens from Shanghai manufacturers such as Weilun, Tianxiang, Xianda, Shengda, Weiyi, Hongfa, Maoye, Dada, Tongyi, Tianyi, Pengchang, Dadong, Danan, Huadong, and Da Zhongguo, as well as the Guohua woolens from Tianjin Fuyuan and the Jin Fuyuan-brand otter woolens and rabbit woolens, are all selling extremely well in Shanghai, with both retail and wholesale transactions being very brisk. Prices range from 1 tael and 3 qian to 3 taels and 7 qian and a half. The first-grade domestic striped camel woolens from various brands are selling for 1 tael and 8 jian, the second grade for 1 tael and 6 qian and a half, the third grade for 1 tael and 5 qian, and the next grade for 1 tael and 1.2 qian. In recent days, various stores have been greatly reducing prices, selling for only 3 jiao and 5 fen per yard.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Discourse

From Lu Genrong and Huang Huiru to the Second Son of the Swedish Crown Prince

— Fo

Since the Lu Genrong and Huang Huiru master-servant love affair occurred, newspapers have been vigorously publicizing it, and society is also paying close attention. I am truly puzzled. Jiangbei Xiaoshanzi and Li Xiuying, eloped together; Zhao Agou and Wang Qiaoyun, committed adultery in a certain hotel. Such news happens countless times every day in Shanghai's dazzling world, but it does not attract attention. Yet, the Lu-Huang case of master-servant love is regarded as a monumental event. This kind of thinking is inevitably somewhat old-fashioned.

All citizens of the Republic of China stand on an equal footing. This seems to be a statement in the Provisional Constitution. Therefore, the terms "master" and "servant" are no longer relevant. Freedom of marriage is also stipulated by the current laws of the Republic of China. Lu Genrong and Huang Huiru's freedom to love was originally a matter of course. However, Lu Genrong is slightly at fault, as he already has a wife at home, which seems to constitute bigamy. In fact, it is only a procedural error. Lu Genrong should have first declared his divorce from his wife and then engaged in this with Huang Huiru, which would have been more justified and legitimate.

The Lu-Huang master-servant love case, as reported in yesterday's newspaper, was declared innocent after a retrial by the Higher Court. This was because the original prosecutor, Jin Henian, disagreed with the verdict and appealed to the Supreme Court. The Supreme Court reviewed and ruled to reject the prosecutor's appeal. Now, Lu Genrong and Huang Huiru are like being granted imperial permission to marry, choosing a partner in court. A young couple can now live together freely, completely free. Therefore, the original prosecutor, Jin Henian, who wanted to cook the crane and burn the zither (separate the lovebirds), was guilty. The Supreme Court, by acting on behalf of heaven and rejecting the appeal, truly accumulated merit like building a pagoda.

Some say that although the Supreme Court rejected the appeal, it only recognized that Lu Genrong was not guilty of theft and did not recognize that Lu and Huang had the status of husband and wife and could cohabitate freely. But who is going to settle this account now? Others say that Lu Genrong still has a plain-looking wife at home, and the wife might become furious. In fact, Lu Genrong's wife is completely a village woman. She sees that her husband has brought back a charming and beautiful lady, and she feels very honored. Of course, she will voluntarily retreat, and she wouldn't dare to be jealous of the young lady.

The minds of our countrymen are so old-fashioned, and the minds of foreigners are even more severely old-fashioned. As reported in yesterday's newspaper, the second son of the Swedish Crown Prince, Lennart, married the daughter of a businessman in London in March of this year, thereby losing his royal rights. The old-fashioned thinking of foreigners is evident here. Now, Lennart plans to open a theater in Stockholm, manage it himself, and serve as the protagonist in the plays. Lennart is willing to be deprived of his royal rights and marry a businesswoman. Originally, (it is easy to find priceless treasures, but difficult to find a true lover). I deeply admire Lennart's courage. I wonder if several gentlemen who read the newspaper, if they encountered such an either/or event, would be willing to be Lennart or willing to be the second son of the Crown Prince. I dare to ask.

Literature and Art

Cricket Fighting

— Ran Nong

White dew falls lightly on the cassia courtyard east,

Stern autumn's chilling air reaches even tiny insects.

Angrily spreading golden wings, rushing to the enemy,

Using silver pincers, establishing warlike merit.

Let me chirp once, boasting of decisive victory,

Laughing at his scattering, timid and unheroic.

The ruins of Banxian Hall retain traces of the past,

Misleading the nation, a thousand years of resentment towards the Prime Minister.

Airplane

Why are there armored soldiers in the silver river?

The cunning of the Qigui chariot lets it run rampant.

Wings like a roc, soaring healthy in the sky,

Body like a dragonfly, lightly touching the water's surface.

Faintly, Chang'e rushes to the moon,

Drifting, Liezi rides the wind.

Galloping three thousand miles a day on the cloud road,

Surely listening to the music of the heavens.

Science

Etching (Continued)

— Shen Shui

Two, Silk Fabric Etching Method

The etching method for silk fabrics is roughly the same as for wool fabrics, and the etching agents used are also similar. Among them, hydrosulfite is the most common and important. However, tin salt etching agents are often used in color etching agents because tin salts can make colors lively and bright, so they are often used. Examples of their formulations are given below:

(A) Hydrosulfite Etching Agent

Hydrosulfite | 175 grams, British gum | 350 grams, water | 600 grams,

After printing, it only needs to be steam-bathed for five minutes to be taken out and washed clean.

(B) Tin Salt Color Etching Agent

Dye | 20 grams, vinegar | 120 grams

, gum water | 700 grams, tin salt | 100 grams, ammonia sulfate | 30 grams, citric acid | 20 grams,

After printing, it must be steam-bathed for half an hour before it can be taken out and washed clean.

Three, Cotton Fabric Etching

Cotton fabrics are most widely used, but we must also try our best to make them beautiful. Their dyeing method is also easier, so many dyes can be dyed on them, such as basic dyes, sulfide dyes, etc. Therefore, the chemical action of the added etching agent is also different, and different etching agents must be used to cope with them. There are many kinds, and now I can only talk about these two:

(1) Etching of Basic Dyes

Hydrosulfite cannot etch many basic dyes, so a chlorate must be used, which is very easy to etch basic dyes. However, if it is not used properly, it can easily damage the fabric. Now there is a kind of potassium sulfite that will not damage the fibers of the fabric. Now let's write the proportion of the ingredients below:

Potassium sulfite | 600 grams, British gum | 300 grams, water | 60 grams, concentrated caustic soda solution | 60 grams, sodium acetate | 20 grams,

Etch well, evaporate for five minutes, and it's good to wash it clean. The only disadvantage is that the application is not very wide. Among the basic dyes that can be etched, there are only magenta, blue, and peacock green and other colors.

(2) Etching of Sulfide Dyes

Many cloths are dyed with sulfide dyes, so its usage is simple and very durable. If you use hydrosulfite and tin salt etching to etch, it will oxidize again during washing, restoring its original color, so more chlorate alum etching agent is used. The formula is as follows:

British gum | 250 grams, chlorate alum solution 600 grams, sodium chlorate | 170 grams, potassium ferrocyanide | 175 grams,

If you want color etching, then the pigments used must be Fuji pigments such as chrome yellow, chrome orange, cinnabar, etc. can all be applied, except for these, they are not suitable. (End)

Improvement Society Discussion

Should Lian Jun's Sunday Holiday Be Abolished?

— Zhen Zhi

I previously published a suggestion in this column to abolish school Sunday holidays. The topic specifically marks the school

Page 21

out, precisely because it is different from other occupations. For other occupations, the abolition of Sunday holidays is also harmful to society, but it is a secondary issue rather than a fundamental one. Lian Jun also clearly understood this sentiment in his article "Should Sunday Be Abolished?" published in this column yesterday, and explained my intention, saying that Zhen Zhi's intention is that our country cannot be strong because science is not prosperous. The reason science is not prosperous is that the people's level of knowledge is low. The reason the people's level of knowledge is low is that the people lack effort in learning. If you want the people to put in more effort, then the abolition of holidays is appropriate. Unexpectedly, the following text reverses the direction of "changing the strings and swiftly providing relief" and opposes the abolition of Sunday, and the topic only mentions "Should Sunday Be Abolished?", which, like the cited Russian newspaper, seems to have nothing to do with schools.

Countries that implement the Sunday holiday system produce talents in large numbers. In ancient times, our country did not implement the Sunday holiday system, but it also produced talents. If teachers do not have Sunday holidays, their lives will be very dull. I don't know if Confucius taught people tirelessly, but was there Sunday at that time? If you want teachers not to be dull and do not seek the progress of students, then holidays can be increased, so why bother to imitate Europe and the United States? Our country's national humiliation days are increasing every year. When we encounter them, we must take a holiday to express our condolences, which should also feel the need for dullness. Lian Jun also said that it is particularly obvious in a certain imperialist country with the most religious overtones, as mentioned by Zhen Zhi. Zhen Zhi has never said this, and I dare not take credit for it. Science is not prosperous, not because of the harm of Sunday holidays, but because of the improper handling of Sunday by the general public. I am not very knowledgeable about what the word "handling" means here. I will tentatively interpret it as "placement." Then Lian Jun is a practitioner of the new calendar. Furthermore, tentatively interpret it as the word "action." I originally advocated the abolition because the people of the country do not use it well and cannot use it well. It is not because of choking and abolishing food. In European and American countries, they first used Sunday holidays as a religious system, which has nothing to do with the material civilization of science. Later, science became prosperous, and Sunday holidays were sufficient to assist the development of science. Looking back at our country, how is the construction? How is science? If we do not increase the time to seek knowledge and increase production at this time, and implement the Sunday holiday system, then we are running counter to each other.

As for saying that the abolition is harmful to students, the reason is that low-ability students can use their holiday time to put more effort into their homework in order to catch up with the smart ones. If this kind of self-taught without a teacher is possible, then why do teachers need to exist, and why do schools need to exist? Because Sunday holidays are harmful to vocational studies, otherwise, why would Soviet Russia change to a continuous work week? The cited Soviet Russian newspapers testify that the meaning in it is biased towards the views of couples following each other and filial piety towards parents. It should be known that these things can be done anytime and anywhere and cannot be said to be a reason for opposition, which is tantamount to exposing one's own shortcomings.

However, since it is a discussion society, there should be repeated refutations of the proposed opinions, which further demonstrates the soundness of the discussion society and the value of the proposed opinions. Lian Jun's intention is not too critical. I am afraid that the people's knowledge is shallow and their prejudice will be increased by Lian Jun's words.

Family

A Domestic All-Out Brawl

— Jing Yu

The neighbor Mr. Huang's family, the day before yesterday afternoon, the Yan family, young and old, played an all-out brawl, causing chaos in the house, and the surrounding people could not rest.

Mr. Huang is from a well-off family, with a wife and a concubine, and above him is an old mother, and below him are children. Among ordinary people, he can be considered blessed!

His wife was also married from a wealthy family. After entering the house, she gave birth to several daughters. She was eager for a son, so she encouraged her husband to bring back her family's maid, A Ying, and take her as a concubine.

She helped her husband marry a mistress, and at the same time, she became pregnant herself. After ten months of pregnancy, she actually gave birth to a son in one fell swoop. (Having a son is the most satisfying thing) The joy in her heart can be imagined.

From then on, she became arrogant and often humiliated A Ying. The old lady did not approve of her behavior and loved A Ying especially. Therefore, conflicts often arose between the wife, concubine, and daughter-in-law. Mr. Huang mediated among them and took his wife and children to live in another residence, so that A Ying could live with the old lady in the old house and serve her day and night.

Mr. Huang's eldest daughter, Miss Xian, was studying at XX middle school. The day before yesterday, she asked for leave to return home and went to her grandmother's place to ask about her well-being. The old lady asked her to have lunch, and everyone ate at the same table. A Ying ate a bowl and got up to add rice at the side table. Miss Xian secretly used her toes to hook the stool she was sitting on under the table. A Ying came back with rice and, without paying attention, sat on empty air, fell, and broke the rice bowl into pieces. She was so ashamed that she didn't know whether to cry or laugh. She couldn't help but curse:

(Pimping my mother, who moved my stool?) In fact, she also knew that it was Miss Xian's mischief, but she didn't want to expose it in person. However, Miss Xian was not willing to show weakness and immediately questioned her sternly:

(You want to pimp my mother? My mother is over there, I'll drag you to pimp her!) While saying this, she started to drag her and slapped her. How could A Ying give up? She also returned the slap. So you dragged me, and I pulled you, twisting into a ball.

Miss Xian's mother got the news and rushed over immediately to help her daughter participate in the battle. The old lady saw that A Ying's two fists could not defeat four hands and was afraid that she would suffer. She pretended to dissuade them, but secretly pulled the mother and daughter's elbows and helped A Ying. At this time, the family of four got into a pile and fought so hard that flowers and water fell, and the bowls on the table were also broken into snowflakes. Later, Mr. Huang saw that the noise was too much and it spread out, which was not decent. He had no choice but to act as an intermediary and mediate between the two sides. He apologized to his mother and wife on behalf of the other. They simply shouted a few times and remained silent. This storm of overturning rivers and seas finally subsided!

A Corner of Society

Enthusiastic People Attract Too Much Trouble

— Shi Ben

Zhang and Li were the closest friends in school. No matter what happened, everyone exchanged information and helped each other, so their friendship could be said to be as close as brothers!

In the last quarter of last year, both of them graduated from XX middle school. Because they were both from poor families, they could not afford to go to school and were busy looking for jobs to solve the bread problem. Soon, Zhang found a position in the business world. Li did not find an opportunity and had to stay at home. Their families were close to each other, so when Zhang set out, he solemnly asked Li to take care of his family. Li also readily agreed, so Zhang went out, and Li often went to Zhang's house to see if his family was safe and sound. He would write a letter to Zhang to report everything he knew, so that he could feel at ease in a foreign land and also show that he had not failed his confidant's entrustment! One day, Li went to Zhang's house and found that Zhang's wife had improper behavior, and the rumors outside were also rampant. He thought that Zhang had repeatedly asked him to pay attention to everything, no matter how big or small, and report it to him. Now that he had discovered this unfortunate event concerning his own reputation, he had to write to him immediately, and he also heard that the adulterer was a famous local hooligan, so he should warn him to be prepared, lest something go wrong. So he wrote a quick letter, reporting everything in detail, and also persuaded him to be optimistic, not to be sad, and hoped that he would quickly find a way to deal with this unfortunate matter!

Zhang received this shocking report like a bolt from the blue. He was filled with jealousy and immediately returned home as fast as he could. When he got home, he questioned her. Of course, she denied it outright and also inquired about the source of his information!

He stayed at home for a few days. His wife had mysterious methods and sweet words, and she probed him for this information on the pillow. After a burst of sweet talk, he honestly told her what Li had reported. When she heard that it was Li's report, she hated Li to the core and came up with a brilliant plan to shift the blame to others. She said to him: (How can you believe Lao Li's nonsense? He has bad intentions himself and often comes to flirt with me. I scolded him several times, so he used this vicious method to retaliate. You are confused and fell for his trick!) When he heard this, he believed it to be true and immediately transferred his hatred for her to Li!

In a few days, he was actually instigated by her and sued Li in court for attempted rape and defamation, and used the letter Li gave him as evidence. When Li learned of this news, he was so angry (that he ate coptis with a mute, unable to express his suffering). He deeply regretted being enthusiastic, which led to attracting trouble. This matter has not been resolved yet. I think in today's world, only (everyone sweeps the snow in front of their own door and does not care about the frost on other people's roofs) can avoid causing trouble. The above matter of Li is also a clear proof! Because this matter can serve as a warning to young people who are not careful in handling affairs, so I record it.

Such a Family

Sacrifice

— Wu

After Mr. Li died, the Li family's household affairs were completely controlled by the eldest son. Of course, the younger siblings had to obey him under the creed of (the eldest brother is like a father), and even the old Mrs. Li obeyed him in accordance with the ancient teachings of (a wife follows her son after her husband dies). Then this eldest son of the Li family had in fact become the head of the family.

The eldest son of the Li family knew very well how to use his authority. This was the most intelligent and proud thing about him. For example, regarding the marriage of his second sister, he dared to insist on his own opinion to his mother:

(In any case, the second sister has to get married, so Mr. Luo, although he is a little older, has a lifelong support, and he doesn't have to worry about eating or living. Isn't that okay?)

So the mother had to say gently:

(But you have to know that your sister is not willing after all!)

(But I have already promised him, because he is my best friend.)

The young master walked out angrily, leaving the old mother to shed tears as she watched his back. She thought:

(How can my daughter marry a businessman in his thirties who already has several children? Is it possible that no one wants my girl?)

So the mother watched her daughter shed tears, and the second young lady cried bitterly in the arms of old Mrs. Li. It was hard for the mother to hold back her tears and say:

(Child! Although Mr. Luo's family wealth is several times better than ours, he is too old and has been married before. Of course, I don't want you to marry him either, but your eldest brother has already allowed him... How can I say anything? If your father were still alive, it wouldn't be like this!)

As she spoke, tears poured down like rain again. Afterwards, she sobbed again and said:

(This is just your fate, what can a mother do?)

Poor second young lady just cried and entangled her mother as she cried.

In the end, the mother and daughter succumbed (under the pressure of the head of the family).

Plaintiff Lu Jingye sues Wu Heming et al. for fraud and embezzlement case (Ruling)

Wu Ruqing is fined two hundred yuan for the crime of fraud. If imprisonment is substituted for the fine, one day of imprisonment shall be substituted for every two yuan. The trial proceedings for Wu Heming, Wu Zhijia, and Yan Baoxiang are suspended. Zheng Xitang is found not guilty. The incidental civil lawsuits are all transferred to the Civil Court for trial.

Police Department sues Yu Afang for intimidation case (Ruling)

Yu Afang is found not guilty.

Police Department sues Shen Hansheng et al. for opium case (Ruling)

Shen Hansheng is sentenced to six months imprisonment for providing a venue for others to smoke opium with the intention of making a profit. Cao Yongsheng is sentenced to two months imprisonment for repeated opium smoking. Xu Jinmao, Kong Aliulu, Xu Wangdai, and Lu Gaoshi are each sentenced to one month imprisonment for opium smoking. The number of days of pre-trial detention shall be offset against the imprisonment term at a rate of two days for one day. Xu Wangshi is found not guilty. Suspended sentences of two years are granted to Kong Aliulu and Cao and Lu Shi. Four opium pipes are confiscated and destroyed.

Police Department sues Ma Peixi et al. for opium case (Ruling)

Ma Peixi is sentenced to three months imprisonment for assisting in providing a venue for others to smoke opium. Chen Baosheng is sentenced to three months imprisonment for repeated opium smoking. Xu Rongfang is sentenced to two months imprisonment for opium smoking. The number of days of pre-trial detention shall be offset against the imprisonment term at a rate of two days for one day. A suspended sentence of two years is granted to Xu Lefang. Opium pipes and dross are confiscated.

Police Department sues Wang Qiaosheng et al. for intimidation and opium, etc. case (Ruling)

Wang Qiaosheng is sentenced to fifteen days detention for the crime of intimidation. The number of days of pre-trial detention shall be offset against the detention term at a rate of two days for one day. Zhu Youfu is sentenced to one month imprisonment for opium smoking. The number of days of pre-trial detention shall be offset against the imprisonment term at a rate of two days for one day. A three-year suspended sentence is granted. Opium paraphernalia is confiscated as per the list.

Police Department sues Zhang Xiangyuan for intimidation case (Ruling)

Zhang Xiangyuan is sentenced to two months imprisonment with a two-year suspended sentence for the crime of jointly intending to unlawfully possess the property of a third party and using intimidation to cause a person to hand over their own property.

Plaintiff, i.e., counter-sued defendant, Zhou Longhai sues Zhou Shi et al. for assault case (Ruling)

Neither the original suit nor the counter-suit are accepted.

Police Department sues Li Xiaoerzi et al. for intimidation case (Ruling)

Li Xiaoerzi and Liu Yongkang are both found not guilty.

Police Department sues Xu Jiabao et al. for fraud case (Ruling)

Xu Jiabao is sentenced to three months imprisonment for each of the two crimes of repeated fraud, with a total sentence of five months imprisonment. Zhu Jintang is sentenced to one month imprisonment for assisting in fraud and two months imprisonment for joint fraud, with a total sentence of two months imprisonment. Zhang Xiangqing is sentenced to two months imprisonment for joint fraud. The number of days of pre-trial detention shall be offset against the imprisonment term at a rate of two days for one day. Four bounced checks are confiscated.

Police Department sues Wu Jinbao et al. for fraud and gambling case (Ruling)

Wu Jinbao is sentenced to two months imprisonment and fined one hundred and twenty yuan for defrauding and obtaining property. Wang Fujin and Yang Yongfu are each sentenced to two months imprisonment and fined sixty yuan for assisting in defrauding and obtaining property. Cai Atang is sentenced to one month imprisonment and fined thirty yuan for assisting in defrauding and obtaining property. If the fines cannot be paid, imprisonment for one day shall be substituted for every two yuan. The number of days of pre-trial detention shall be offset against the fine at a rate of one day for every two yuan. Shen Dakui, Dong Jinchun, Sheng Atu, Wang Qingsheng, Zhang Hairong, and Weng Shunkang are each fined twenty yuan for gambling for property. If the fines cannot be paid, imprisonment for one day shall be substituted for every one yuan. The number of days of pre-trial detention shall be offset against the fine at a rate of one day for every one yuan. Shen Qiaosong and Wu Yousheng are both found not guilty. Gambling money, gambling paraphernalia, and magnets are confiscated as per the list.

Police Department sues Wang Fulin et al. for fraud (Ruling)

Wang Fulin is sentenced to two months imprisonment and fined sixty yuan for defrauding and obtaining property. Li Tongshou is sentenced to two months imprisonment and fined sixty yuan for assisting in defrauding and obtaining property. You Arer is sentenced to three months imprisonment and fined one hundred and twenty yuan for repeatedly assisting in defrauding and obtaining property. If the fines cannot be paid, imprisonment for one day shall be substituted for every two yuan. The number of days of pre-trial detention shall be offset against the imprisonment term at a rate of two days for one day. Gambling paraphernalia, gambling money, and magnets are confiscated as per the list.

Police Department sues Ke Jingui for a theft case (Above are from September 22nd)

▲Civil Judgments▲

Tang Jinyuan et al. sues Ye Ruizhai et al. for debt case (Ruling)

The defendants Luo Buzhou, Zhang Xingbei, You Xiaozhang, Wang Donghai, and Wang Zhenji et al. shall be jointly and severally liable to repay the plaintiffs foreign currency $1,983.826, plus interest at a rate of five percent per annum from the date of the lawsuit until the date of execution. The defendant Ye Ruizhai shall be responsible for clearing and repaying the aforementioned debt. The plaintiffs' request that the defendant Shang Mujiang be jointly and severally liable for the aforementioned debt is rejected. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendants Luo Buzhou et al.; the litigation costs for the part concerning the defendant Shang Mujiang shall be borne by the plaintiffs.

Plaintiff, i.e., counter-sued defendant, Qi Rengxi, and Zhang Meili's case for separation of family relationship (Ruling)

The separation of family relationship between the two parties is approved. All children shall be under the guardianship of the defendant Zhang Meili. The plaintiff Qi Rengxi shall pay child support of foreign currency $500 per month. The litigation costs for the main suit shall be borne by the two parties themselves; the litigation costs for the counter-suit shall be borne by the plaintiff Qi Rengxi for seven-tenths and the defendant Zhang Meili for three-tenths.

Liu Xiubao and Jiang Jinhai's divorce case (Ruling)

The plaintiff's request for divorce is rejected. The defendant shall return to the plaintiff a gold bracelet weighing seven mace and two fen, two gold rings weighing six mace, and a camel hair robe. The litigation costs shall be borne by the two parties themselves.

Qiu Guifu sues Sheng Wonian for payment of wages case (Ruling)

The defendant shall pay the plaintiff foreign currency $85. The plaintiff's remaining requests are rejected. The plaintiff shall bear two-thirds of the litigation costs, and the defendant shall bear one-third.

Haishan, Manager of Lulin Foreign Firm, sues Nanlin Hao et al. for cargo payment case (Ruling)

Cui Jinqing and Li Dasheng shall be jointly and severally liable to repay the plaintiff for Order No. 48 cargo, British gold 67 pounds and 10 shillings, plus interest at a rate of five percent per annum from January 27th of this year until the date of settlement, plus warehouse rent of silver two mace per piece per month from ten days after the arrival of the goods, plus fire insurance calculated at silver three taels per thousand taels per year until the date of settlement, plus labor fees of silver one mace per piece. They shall also be jointly and severally liable to repay the plaintiff for Order No. 288 and Order No. 289 cargo, US dollars $4,032.50, customs duty and special tax customs gold $494.76, plus interest at a rate of five percent per annum on US dollars $2,016.25 from December 30th of last year until the date of settlement, plus interest at a rate of five percent per annum on US dollars $2,016.25 from February 2nd of this year until the date of settlement, plus warehouse rent of silver two mace per piece per month from ten days after the arrival of the goods, plus fire insurance calculated at silver three taels per thousand taels per year until the date of settlement, plus labor fees of silver one mace per piece. The plaintiff's remaining requests are rejected. The litigation costs shall be borne by Cui Jinqing and Li Dasheng. (Above are from September 22nd)

Civil Instructions

A petition from Yezinu for amicable divorce requesting filing.

Having read the petition, the filing is approved. This instruction is issued.

A petition from Wu Jinyun for merger of shares requesting filing.

Having read the petition, there is no evidence to support the claim of a merger, and there is no basis for review. The requested filing is difficult to approve. This instruction is issued.

A petition from Lawyer Yu Hualong requesting a price list for ledgers.

Having read the petition, it is noted that in the case of Quan Changxiang Hao et al. versus Yu Tai Fuji Hao for preservation of evidence, the petitioner obtained eighteen ledgers that were retained by the court. Now, it is stated that the case has been fully settled, and all ledgers previously submitted to the court should be returned. You should come to the court on the morning of the 26th of this month to provide a price. This instruction is issued.

A continued request from Yao Wende's agent, Lawyer Le Junying, for detention and interrogation.

Having read the petition, the court previously scheduled August 25th for the issuance of an arrest warrant, but the creditor did not come to the court to designate the arrest. Now, it is requested again. You should set another date for issuing an order for arrest. This instruction is issued.

A petition from Pan Qizhang requesting to receive funds.

Having read the petition, you should come to the court at 9:00 AM on the 28th of this month to receive the funds. This instruction is issued.

A petition from Tianfa Xie Electrical Firm requesting exemption from sealing.

Having read the petition, since it is stated that an amicable settlement has been reached with the debtor, the request for exemption from sealing should be approved. The submitted sealing fee should be collected from the court at 9:00 AM on the 28th of this month. The enforcement of this case should be stopped immediately, and you should be informed. This instruction is issued.

A petition from Sun Zhuchen et al. requesting the return of clothing.

Having read the petition, it is noted that the creditor has already requested the unsealing of the case. You should be informed immediately. This instruction is issued.

A petition from Zhu Hanzhang requesting unsealing.

Having read the petition, the request is approved. You should order the official to proceed with the unsealing. This instruction is issued.

A petition from Lian Weihan requesting to receive funds.

Having read the petition, you should come to the court at 2:00 PM on the 28th of this month to receive the funds. This instruction is issued.

A petition from Bai Bo Xu requesting to receive funds.

Regarding the request to receive funds, you should invite the debtor to come to the court at 9:00 AM on the 30th of this month to await review and handling. This instruction is issued.

A petition from Sanhe Company requesting revocation of provisional attachment.

Since it is stated that an amicable settlement has been reached, the request for revocation of the provisional attachment should be approved. You should set a date for dispatching personnel to unseal. This instruction is issued.

A petition from Xinghe Company Han Zhisun requesting closure of the case.

The closure of the case is approved. This instruction is issued.

A petition from Tao Guisong requesting to receive funds.

You should come to the court at 10:00 AM on the 26th of this month to receive the funds. This instruction is issued.

A petition from Wu Huaichun requesting closure of the case.

The closure of the case is approved. This instruction is issued. (Above are from September 23rd)

Shanghai Local Court

▲Criminal Court Judgments

Judgment on Wang Guangxiang's Case of Military Firearms and Ammunition (Main Text)

Wang Guangxiang, for possessing military firearms and ammunition without permission, is sentenced to six months of imprisonment. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two days.

Judgment on Liu Shanquan's Murder Case (Main Text)

Liu Shanquan, for murder, is sentenced to twelve years of imprisonment. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two days.

Judgment on the Appeal Case of Yang Hongxi's Adultery by the Procurator of This Court (Main Text)

The appeal is rejected.

Judgment on Yu Dalai, also known as Yu Dalianzi's, Robbery Case (Main Text)

Yu Dalai, for robbing others' property with a gang of three or more people, is sentenced to four years of imprisonment. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two days.

Judgment on Chen Jing et al.'s Malfeasance and Opium Case (Main Text)

Chen Jing, for repeatedly accepting bribes and committing acts that violated his duties, is sentenced to one year and six months of imprisonment, and a fine of two hundred yuan. If the fine is not fully paid after compulsory execution, one day of imprisonment will be substituted for every two yuan. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two days. Chen Jing is found not guilty of embezzlement.

Ding Wangshi, for intending to profit from opening a establishment where people smoke opium, is sentenced to six months of imprisonment and a fine of sixty yuan. If the fine is not fully paid after compulsory execution, one day of imprisonment will be substituted for every one yuan. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two days.

Jin Guisheng, for smoking opium, is sentenced to two months of imprisonment; for delivering bribes to public officials regarding acts that violate their duties, he is sentenced to two months of imprisonment, with a total sentence of three months of imprisonment. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two days. Jin Guisheng is found not guilty of opening an opium den.

Wang Jinsheng, for smoking opium, is sentenced to one month of imprisonment and a fine of forty yuan.

If the fine is not fully paid after compulsory execution, one day of imprisonment will be substituted for every one yuan. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two days.

Shen Fugeng, for helping to deliver bribes to public officials regarding acts that violate their duties, is sentenced to one month of imprisonment.

The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two days.

Four opium pipes and lamps, one opium pot, a jar, and bowls, two opium scales and trays, and another seven items are all confiscated.

Judgment on Li Adi et al.'s Assault and False Accusation Case (Main Text)

Li Adi, for using methods sufficient to cause serious injury and causing injury, the number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two days.

Chai Rui, Meng Xiqing, Jiang Azhang, Gao Hongye, Zhu Lanyong, and others are each sentenced to two months of imprisonment for the crime of aiding in a brawl.

The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two days. Li Adi, Jiang Azhang, and Meng Xiqing are found not guilty of false accusation.

Judgment on Tao Haishan's Theft Case (Main Text)

Tao Haishan, for habitual theft, is sentenced to one year of imprisonment. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two days.

Judgment on Gu Ziyou's Harming Family Case (Main Text)

Gu Ziyou, for the crime of enticing a woman under the age of twenty with the intent of adultery, is sentenced to one year of imprisonment. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two days. The accompanying civil suit is rejected.

Judgment on Su Liansheng's Harming Freedom Case (Main Text)

The public prosecution in this case is not accepted.

Judgment on Chen Zhangqing, i.e., Chen Zhangxiang's, Case of Causing Death by Negligence (Main Text)

Chen Zhangqing, for causing death by negligence in his profession, is sentenced to three months of imprisonment. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two days. The accompanying civil lawsuit is transferred to the civil court of this court for trial. (All of the above on September 22nd)
